<span name="2.1.239">With him! why, 'tis not possible.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.1.240">Lay thy finger thus, and let thy soul be instructed.</span><br>
<span name="2.1.241">Mark me with what violence she first loved the Moor,</span><br>
<span name="2.1.242">but for bragging and telling her fantastical lies:</span><br>
<span name="2.1.243">and will she love him still for prating? let not</span><br>
<span name="2.1.244">thy discreet heart think it. Her eye must be fed;</span><br>
<span name="2.1.245">and what delight shall she have to look on the</span><br>
<span name="2.1.246">devil? When the blood is made dull with the act of</span><br>
<span name="2.1.247">sport, there should be, again to inflame it and to</span><br>
<span name="2.1.248">give satiety a fresh appetite, loveliness in favour,</span><br>
<span name="2.1.249">sympathy in years, manners and beauties; all which</span><br>
<span name="2.1.250">the Moor is defective in: now, for want of these</span><br>
<span name="2.1.251">required conveniences, her delicate tenderness will</span><br>
<span name="2.1.252">find itself abused, begin to heave the gorge,</span><br>
<span name="2.1.253">disrelish and abhor the Moor; very nature will</span><br>
<span name="2.1.254">instruct her in it and compel her to some second</span><br>
<span name="2.1.255">choice. Now, sir, this granted,--as it is a most</span><br>
<span name="2.1.256">pregnant and unforced position--who stands so</span><br>
<span name="2.1.257">eminent in the degree of this fortune as Cassio</span><br>
<span name="2.1.258">does? a knave very voluble; no further</span><br>
<span name="2.1.259">conscionable than in putting on the mere form of</span><br>
<span name="2.1.260">civil and humane seeming, for the better compassing</span><br>
<span name="2.1.261">of his salt and most hidden loose affection? why,</span><br>
<span name="2.1.262">none; why, none: a slipper and subtle knave, a</span><br>
<span name="2.1.263">finder of occasions, that has an eye can stamp and</span><br>
<span name="2.1.264">counterfeit advantages, though true advantage never</span><br>
<span name="2.1.265">present itself; a devilish knave. Besides, the</span><br>
<span name="2.1.266">knave is handsome, young, and hath all those</span><br>
<span name="2.1.267">requisites in him that folly and green minds look</span><br>
<span name="2.1.268">after: a pestilent complete knave; and the woman</span><br>
<span name="2.1.269">hath found him already.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.1.270">I cannot believe that in her; she's full of</span><br>
<span name="2.1.271">most blessed condition.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.1.272">Blessed fig's-end! the wine she drinks is made of</span><br>
<span name="2.1.273">grapes: if she had been blessed, she would never</span><br>
<span name="2.1.274">have loved the Moor. Blessed pudding! Didst thou</span><br>
<span name="2.1.275">not see her paddle with the palm of his hand? didst</span><br>
<span name="2.1.276">not mark that?</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.1.277">Yes, that I did; but that was but courtesy.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.1.278">Lechery, by this hand; an index and obscure prologue</span><br>
<span name="2.1.279">to the history of lust and foul thoughts. They met</span><br>
<span name="2.1.280">so near with their lips that their breaths embraced</span><br>
<span name="2.1.281">together. Villanous thoughts, Roderigo! when these</span><br>
<span name="2.1.282">mutualities so marshal the way, hard at hand comes</span><br>
<span name="2.1.283">the master and main exercise, the incorporate</span><br>
<span name="2.1.284">conclusion, Pish! But, sir, be you ruled by me: I</span><br>
<span name="2.1.285">have brought you from Venice. Watch you to-night;</span><br>
<span name="2.1.286">for the command, I'll lay't upon you. Cassio knows</span><br>
<span name="2.1.287">you not. I'll not be far from you: do you find</span><br>
<span name="2.1.288">some occasion to anger Cassio, either by speaking</span><br>
<span name="2.1.289">too loud, or tainting his discipline; or from what</span><br>
<span name="2.1.290">other course you please, which the time shall more</span><br>
<span name="2.1.291">favourably minister.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.1.292">Well.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.1.293">Sir, he is rash and very sudden in choler, and haply</span><br>
<span name="2.1.294">may strike at you: provoke him, that he may; for</span><br>
<span name="2.1.295">even out of that will I cause these of Cyprus to</span><br>
<span name="2.1.296">mutiny; whose qualification shall come into no true</span><br>
<span name="2.1.297">taste again but by the displanting of Cassio. So</span><br>
<span name="2.1.298">shall you have a shorter journey to your desires by</span><br>
<span name="2.1.299">the means I shall then have to prefer them; and the</span><br>
<span name="2.1.300">impediment most profitably removed, without the</span><br>
<span name="2.1.301">which there were no expectation of our prosperity.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.1.302">I will do this, if I can bring it to any</span><br>
<span name="2.1.303">opportunity.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.1.304">I warrant thee. Meet me by and by at the citadel:</span><br>
<span name="2.1.305">I must fetch his necessaries ashore. Farewell.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.1.306">Adieu.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.1.307">That Cassio loves her, I do well believe it;</span><br>
<span name="2.1.308">That she loves him, 'tis apt and of great credit:</span><br>
<span name="2.1.309">The Moor, howbeit that I endure him not,</span><br>
<span name="2.1.310">Is of a constant, loving, noble nature,</span><br>
<span name="2.1.311">And I dare think he'll prove to Desdemona</span><br>
<span name="2.1.312">A most dear husband. Now, I do love her too;</span><br>
<span name="2.1.313">Not out of absolute lust, though peradventure</span><br>
<span name="2.1.314">I stand accountant for as great a sin,</span><br>
<span name="2.1.315">But partly led to diet my revenge,</span><br>
<span name="2.1.316">For that I do suspect the lusty Moor</span><br>
<span name="2.1.317">Hath leap'd into my seat; the thought whereof</span><br>
<span name="2.1.318">Doth, like a poisonous mineral, gnaw my inwards;</span><br>
<span name="2.1.319">And nothing can or shall content my soul</span><br>
<span name="2.1.320">Till I am even'd with him, wife for wife,</span><br>
<span name="2.1.321">Or failing so, yet that I put the Moor</span><br>
<span name="2.1.322">At least into a jealousy so strong</span><br>
<span name="2.1.323">That judgment cannot cure. Which thing to do,</span><br>
<span name="2.1.324">If this poor trash of Venice, whom I trash</span><br>
<span name="2.1.325">For his quick hunting, stand the putting on,</span><br>
<span name="2.1.326">I'll have our Michael Cassio on the hip,</span><br>
<span name="2.1.327">Abuse him to the Moor in the rank garb--</span><br>
<span name="2.1.328">For I fear Cassio with my night-cap too--</span><br>
<span name="2.1.329">Make the Moor thank me, love me and reward me.</span><br>
<span name="2.1.330">For making him egregiously an ass</span><br>
<span name="2.1.331">And practising upon his peace and quiet</span><br>
<span name="2.1.332">Even to madness. 'Tis here, but yet confused:</span><br>
<span name="2.1.333">Knavery's plain face is never seen tin used.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<br>
<h3>SCENE II. A street.</h3>
<p></p><br>
<i>Enter a Herald with a proclamation; People following</i>
<br>

<b>Herald</b>
<br>
<span name="2.2.1">It is Othello's pleasure, our noble and valiant</span><br>
<span name="2.2.2">general, that, upon certain tidings now arrived,</span><br>
<span name="2.2.3">importing the mere perdition of the Turkish fleet,</span><br>
<span name="2.2.4">every man put himself into triumph; some to dance,</span><br>
<span name="2.2.5">some to make bonfires, each man to what sport and</span><br>
<span name="2.2.6">revels his addiction leads him: for, besides these</span><br>
<span name="2.2.7">beneficial news, it is the celebration of his</span><br>
<span name="2.2.8">nuptial. So much was his pleasure should be</span><br>
<span name="2.2.9">proclaimed. All offices are open, and there is full</span><br>
<span name="2.2.10">liberty of feasting from this present hour of five</span><br>
<span name="2.2.11">till the bell have told eleven. Heaven bless the</span><br>
<span name="2.2.12">isle of Cyprus and our noble general Othello!</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
<br>
<h3>SCENE III. A hall in the castle.</h3>
<p></p><br>
<i>Enter OTHELLO, DESDEMONA, CASSIO, and Attendants</i>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.1">Good Michael, look you to the guard to-night:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.2">Let's teach ourselves that honourable stop,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.3">Not to outsport discretion.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.4">Iago hath direction what to do;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.5">But, notwithstanding, with my personal eye</span><br>
<span name="2.3.6">Will I look to't.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.7">                  Iago is most honest.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.8">Michael, good night: to-morrow with your earliest</span><br>
<span name="2.3.9">Let me have speech with you.</span><br>
<p><i>To DESDEMONA</i></p>
<span name="2.3.10">Come, my dear love,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.11">The purchase made, the fruits are to ensue;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.12">That profit's yet to come 'tween me and you.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.13">Good night.</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt OTHELLO, DESDEMONA, and Attendants</i></p>
<p><i>Enter IAGO</i></p>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.14">Welcome, Iago; we must to the watch.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.15">Not this hour, lieutenant; 'tis not yet ten o' the</span><br>
<span name="2.3.16">clock. Our general cast us thus early for the love</span><br>
<span name="2.3.17">of his Desdemona; who let us not therefore blame:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.18">he hath not yet made wanton the night with her; and</span><br>
<span name="2.3.19">she is sport for Jove.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.20">She's a most exquisite lady.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.21">And, I'll warrant her, fun of game.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.22">Indeed, she's a most fresh and delicate creature.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.23">What an eye she has! methinks it sounds a parley of</span><br>
<span name="2.3.24">provocation.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.25">An inviting eye; and yet methinks right modest.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.26">And when she speaks, is it not an alarum to love?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.27">She is indeed perfection.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.28">Well, happiness to their sheets! Come, lieutenant, I</span><br>
<span name="2.3.29">have a stoup of wine; and here without are a brace</span><br>
<span name="2.3.30">of Cyprus gallants that would fain have a measure to</span><br>
<span name="2.3.31">the health of black Othello.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.32">Not to-night, good Iago: I have very poor and</span><br>
<span name="2.3.33">unhappy brains for drinking: I could well wish</span><br>
<span name="2.3.34">courtesy would invent some other custom of</span><br>
<span name="2.3.35">entertainment.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.36">O, they are our friends; but one cup: I'll drink for</span><br>
<span name="2.3.37">you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.38">I have drunk but one cup to-night, and that was</span><br>
<span name="2.3.39">craftily qualified too, and, behold, what innovation</span><br>
<span name="2.3.40">it makes here: I am unfortunate in the infirmity,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.41">and dare not task my weakness with any more.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.42">What, man! 'tis a night of revels: the gallants</span><br>
<span name="2.3.43">desire it.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.44">Where are they?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.45">Here at the door; I pray you, call them in.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.46">I'll do't; but it dislikes me.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.47">If I can fasten but one cup upon him,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.48">With that which he hath drunk to-night already,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.49">He'll be as full of quarrel and offence</span><br>
<span name="2.3.50">As my young mistress' dog. Now, my sick fool Roderigo,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.51">Whom love hath turn'd almost the wrong side out,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.52">To Desdemona hath to-night caroused</span><br>
<span name="2.3.53">Potations pottle-deep; and he's to watch:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.54">Three lads of Cyprus, noble swelling spirits,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.55">That hold their honours in a wary distance,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.56">The very elements of this warlike isle,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.57">Have I to-night fluster'd with flowing cups,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.58">And they watch too. Now, 'mongst this flock of drunkards,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.59">Am I to put our Cassio in some action</span><br>
<span name="2.3.60">That may offend the isle.--But here they come:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.61">If consequence do but approve my dream,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.62">My boat sails freely, both with wind and stream.</span><br>
<p><i>Re-enter CASSIO; with him MONTANO and Gentlemen; servants following with wine</i></p>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.63">'Fore God, they have given me a rouse already.</span><br>
<br>

<b>MONTANO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.64">Good faith, a little one; not past a pint, as I am</span><br>
<span name="2.3.65">a soldier.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.66">Some wine, ho!</span><br>
<p><i>Sings</i></p>
<span name="2.3.67">And let me the canakin clink, clink;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.68">And let me the canakin clink</span><br>
<span name="2.3.69">A soldier's a man;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.70">A life's but a span;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.71">Why, then, let a soldier drink.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.72">Some wine, boys!</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.73">'Fore God, an excellent song.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.74">I learned it in England, where, indeed, they are</span><br>
<span name="2.3.75">most potent in potting: your Dane, your German, and</span><br>
<span name="2.3.76">your swag-bellied Hollander--Drink, ho!--are nothing</span><br>
<span name="2.3.77">to your English.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.78">Is your Englishman so expert in his drinking?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.79">Why, he drinks you, with facility, your Dane dead</span><br>
<span name="2.3.80">drunk; he sweats not to overthrow your Almain; he</span><br>
<span name="2.3.81">gives your Hollander a vomit, ere the next pottle</span><br>
<span name="2.3.82">can be filled.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.83">To the health of our general!</span><br>
<br>

<b>MONTANO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.84">I am for it, lieutenant; and I'll do you justice.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.85">O sweet England!</span><br>
<span name="2.3.86">King Stephen was a worthy peer,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.87">His breeches cost him but a crown;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.88">He held them sixpence all too dear,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.89">With that he call'd the tailor lown.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.90">He was a wight of high renown,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.91">And thou art but of low degree:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.92">'Tis pride that pulls the country down;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.93">Then take thine auld cloak about thee.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.94">Some wine, ho!</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.95">Why, this is a more exquisite song than the other.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.96">Will you hear't again?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.97">No; for I hold him to be unworthy of his place that</span><br>
<span name="2.3.98">does those things. Well, God's above all; and there</span><br>
<span name="2.3.99">be souls must be saved, and there be souls must not be saved.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.100">It's true, good lieutenant.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.101">For mine own part,--no offence to the general, nor</span><br>
<span name="2.3.102">any man of quality,--I hope to be saved.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.103">And so do I too, lieutenant.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.104">Ay, but, by your leave, not before me; the</span><br>
<span name="2.3.105">lieutenant is to be saved before the ancient. Let's</span><br>
<span name="2.3.106">have no more of this; let's to our affairs.--Forgive</span><br>
<span name="2.3.107">us our sins!--Gentlemen, let's look to our business.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.108">Do not think, gentlemen. I am drunk: this is my</span><br>
<span name="2.3.109">ancient; this is my right hand, and this is my left:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.110">I am not drunk now; I can stand well enough, and</span><br>
<span name="2.3.111">speak well enough.</span><br>
<br>

<b>All</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.112">Excellent well.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.113">Why, very well then; you must not think then that I am drunk.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<br>

<b>MONTANO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.114">To the platform, masters; come, let's set the watch.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.115">You see this fellow that is gone before;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.116">He is a soldier fit to stand by Caesar</span><br>
<span name="2.3.117">And give direction: and do but see his vice;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.118">'Tis to his virtue a just equinox,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.119">The one as long as the other: 'tis pity of him.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.120">I fear the trust Othello puts him in.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.121">On some odd time of his infirmity,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.122">Will shake this island.</span><br>
<br>

<b>MONTANO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.123">But is he often thus?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.124">'Tis evermore the prologue to his sleep:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.125">He'll watch the horologe a double set,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.126">If drink rock not his cradle.</span><br>
<br>

<b>MONTANO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.127">It were well</span><br>
<span name="2.3.128">The general were put in mind of it.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.129">Perhaps he sees it not; or his good nature</span><br>
<span name="2.3.130">Prizes the virtue that appears in Cassio,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.131">And looks not on his evils: is not this true?</span><br>
<p><i>Enter RODERIGO</i></p>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.132">[Aside to him]  How now, Roderigo!</span><br>
<span name="2.3.133">I pray you, after the lieutenant; go.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit RODERIGO</i></p>
<br>

<b>MONTANO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.134">And 'tis great pity that the noble Moor</span><br>
<span name="2.3.135">Should hazard such a place as his own second</span><br>
<span name="2.3.136">With one of an ingraft infirmity:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.137">It were an honest action to say</span><br>
<span name="2.3.138">So to the Moor.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.139">                  Not I, for this fair island:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.140">I do love Cassio well; and would do much</span><br>
<span name="2.3.141">To cure him of this evil--But, hark! what noise?</span><br>
<p><i>Cry within: 'Help! help!'</i></p>
<p><i>Re-enter CASSIO, driving in RODERIGO</i></p>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.142">You rogue! you rascal!</span><br>
<br>

<b>MONTANO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.143">What's the matter, lieutenant?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.144">A knave teach me my duty!</span><br>
<span name="2.3.145">I'll beat the knave into a twiggen bottle.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.146">Beat me!</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.147">       Dost thou prate, rogue?</span><br>
<p><i>Striking RODERIGO</i></p>
<br>

<b>MONTANO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.148">Nay, good lieutenant;</span><br>
<p><i>Staying him</i></p>
<span name="2.3.149">I pray you, sir, hold your hand.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.150">Let me go, sir,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.151">Or I'll knock you o'er the mazzard.</span><br>
<br>

<b>MONTANO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.152">Come, come,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.153">you're drunk.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.154">Drunk!</span><br>
<p><i>They fight</i></p>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.155">[Aside to RODERIGO]  Away, I say; go out, and cry a mutiny.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit RODERIGO</i></p>
<span name="2.3.156">Nay, good lieutenant,--alas, gentlemen;--</span><br>
<span name="2.3.157">Help, ho!--Lieutenant,--sir,--Montano,--sir;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.158">Help, masters!--Here's a goodly watch indeed!</span><br>
<p><i>Bell rings</i></p>
<span name="2.3.159">Who's that which rings the bell?--Diablo, ho!</span><br>
<span name="2.3.160">The town will rise: God's will, lieutenant, hold!</span><br>
<span name="2.3.161">You will be shamed for ever.</span><br>
<p><i>Re-enter OTHELLO and Attendants</i></p>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.162">What is the matter here?</span><br>
<br>

<b>MONTANO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.163">'Zounds, I bleed still; I am hurt to the death.</span><br>
<p><i>Faints</i></p>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.164">Hold, for your lives!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.165">Hold, ho! Lieutenant,--sir--Montano,--gentlemen,--</span><br>
<span name="2.3.166">Have you forgot all sense of place and duty?</span><br>
<span name="2.3.167">Hold! the general speaks to you; hold, hold, for shame!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.168">Why, how now, ho! from whence ariseth this?</span><br>
<span name="2.3.169">Are we turn'd Turks, and to ourselves do that</span><br>
<span name="2.3.170">Which heaven hath forbid the Ottomites?</span><br>
<span name="2.3.171">For Christian shame, put by this barbarous brawl:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.172">He that stirs next to carve for his own rage</span><br>
<span name="2.3.173">Holds his soul light; he dies upon his motion.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.174">Silence that dreadful bell: it frights the isle</span><br>
<span name="2.3.175">From her propriety. What is the matter, masters?</span><br>
<span name="2.3.176">Honest Iago, that look'st dead with grieving,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.177">Speak, who began this? on thy love, I charge thee.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.178">I do not know: friends all but now, even now,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.179">In quarter, and in terms like bride and groom</span><br>
<span name="2.3.180">Devesting them for bed; and then, but now--</span><br>
<span name="2.3.181">As if some planet had unwitted men--</span><br>
<span name="2.3.182">Swords out, and tilting one at other's breast,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.183">In opposition bloody. I cannot speak</span><br>
<span name="2.3.184">Any beginning to this peevish odds;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.185">And would in action glorious I had lost</span><br>
<span name="2.3.186">Those legs that brought me to a part of it!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.187">How comes it, Michael, you are thus forgot?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.188">I pray you, pardon me; I cannot speak.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.189">Worthy Montano, you were wont be civil;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.190">The gravity and stillness of your youth</span><br>
<span name="2.3.191">The world hath noted, and your name is great</span><br>
<span name="2.3.192">In mouths of wisest censure: what's the matter,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.193">That you unlace your reputation thus</span><br>
<span name="2.3.194">And spend your rich opinion for the name</span><br>
<span name="2.3.195">Of a night-brawler? give me answer to it.</span><br>
<br>

<b>MONTANO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.196">Worthy Othello, I am hurt to danger:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.197">Your officer, Iago, can inform you,--</span><br>
<span name="2.3.198">While I spare speech, which something now</span><br>
<span name="2.3.199">offends me,--</span><br>
<span name="2.3.200">Of all that I do know: nor know I aught</span><br>
<span name="2.3.201">By me that's said or done amiss this night;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.202">Unless self-charity be sometimes a vice,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.203">And to defend ourselves it be a sin</span><br>
<span name="2.3.204">When violence assails us.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.205">Now, by heaven,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.206">My blood begins my safer guides to rule;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.207">And passion, having my best judgment collied,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.208">Assays to lead the way: if I once stir,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.209">Or do but lift this arm, the best of you</span><br>
<span name="2.3.210">Shall sink in my rebuke. Give me to know</span><br>
<span name="2.3.211">How this foul rout began, who set it on;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.212">And he that is approved in this offence,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.213">Though he had twinn'd with me, both at a birth,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.214">Shall lose me. What! in a town of war,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.215">Yet wild, the people's hearts brimful of fear,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.216">To manage private and domestic quarrel,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.217">In night, and on the court and guard of safety!</span><br>
<span name="2.3.218">'Tis monstrous. Iago, who began't?</span><br>
<br>

<b>MONTANO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.219">If partially affined, or leagued in office,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.220">Thou dost deliver more or less than truth,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.221">Thou art no soldier.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.222">Touch me not so near:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.223">I had rather have this tongue cut from my mouth</span><br>
<span name="2.3.224">Than it should do offence to Michael Cassio;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.225">Yet, I persuade myself, to speak the truth</span><br>
<span name="2.3.226">Shall nothing wrong him. Thus it is, general.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.227">Montano and myself being in speech,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.228">There comes a fellow crying out for help:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.229">And Cassio following him with determined sword,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.230">To execute upon him. Sir, this gentleman</span><br>
<span name="2.3.231">Steps in to Cassio, and entreats his pause:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.232">Myself the crying fellow did pursue,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.233">Lest by his clamour--as it so fell out--</span><br>
<span name="2.3.234">The town might fall in fright: he, swift of foot,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.235">Outran my purpose; and I return'd the rather</span><br>
<span name="2.3.236">For that I heard the clink and fall of swords,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.237">And Cassio high in oath; which till to-night</span><br>
<span name="2.3.238">I ne'er might say before. When I came back--</span><br>
<span name="2.3.239">For this was brief--I found them close together,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.240">At blow and thrust; even as again they were</span><br>
<span name="2.3.241">When you yourself did part them.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.242">More of this matter cannot I report:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.243">But men are men; the best sometimes forget:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.244">Though Cassio did some little wrong to him,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.245">As men in rage strike those that wish them best,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.246">Yet surely Cassio, I believe, received</span><br>
<span name="2.3.247">From him that fled some strange indignity,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.248">Which patience could not pass.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.249">I know, Iago,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.250">Thy honesty and love doth mince this matter,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.251">Making it light to Cassio. Cassio, I love thee</span><br>
<span name="2.3.252">But never more be officer of mine.</span><br>
<p><i>Re-enter DESDEMONA, attended</i></p>
<span name="2.3.253">Look, if my gentle love be not raised up!</span><br>
<span name="2.3.254">I'll make thee an example.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.255">What's the matter?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.256">All's well now, sweeting; come away to bed.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.257">Sir, for your hurts, myself will be your surgeon:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.258">Lead him off.</span><br>
<p><i>To MONTANO, who is led off</i></p>
<span name="2.3.259">Iago, look with care about the town,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.260">And silence those whom this vile brawl distracted.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.261">Come, Desdemona: 'tis the soldiers' life</span><br>
<span name="2.3.262">To have their balmy slumbers waked with strife.</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt all but IAGO and CASSIO</i></p>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.263">What, are you hurt, lieutenant?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.264">Ay, past all surgery.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.265">Marry, heaven forbid!</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.266">Reputation, reputation, reputation! O, I have lost</span><br>
<span name="2.3.267">my reputation! I have lost the immortal part of</span><br>
<span name="2.3.268">myself, and what remains is bestial. My reputation,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.269">Iago, my reputation!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.270">As I am an honest man, I thought you had received</span><br>
<span name="2.3.271">some bodily wound; there is more sense in that than</span><br>
<span name="2.3.272">in reputation. Reputation is an idle and most false</span><br>
<span name="2.3.273">imposition: oft got without merit, and lost without</span><br>
<span name="2.3.274">deserving: you have lost no reputation at all,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.275">unless you repute yourself such a loser. What, man!</span><br>
<span name="2.3.276">there are ways to recover the general again: you</span><br>
<span name="2.3.277">are but now cast in his mood, a punishment more in</span><br>
<span name="2.3.278">policy than in malice, even so as one would beat his</span><br>
<span name="2.3.279">offenceless dog to affright an imperious lion: sue</span><br>
<span name="2.3.280">to him again, and he's yours.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.281">I will rather sue to be despised than to deceive so</span><br>
<span name="2.3.282">good a commander with so slight, so drunken, and so</span><br>
<span name="2.3.283">indiscreet an officer. Drunk? and speak parrot?</span><br>
<span name="2.3.284">and squabble? swagger? swear? and discourse</span><br>
<span name="2.3.285">fustian with one's own shadow? O thou invisible</span><br>
<span name="2.3.286">spirit of wine, if thou hast no name to be known by,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.287">let us call thee devil!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.288">What was he that you followed with your sword? What</span><br>
<span name="2.3.289">had he done to you?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.290">I know not.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.291">Is't possible?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.292">I remember a mass of things, but nothing distinctly;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.293">a quarrel, but nothing wherefore. O God, that men</span><br>
<span name="2.3.294">should put an enemy in their mouths to steal away</span><br>
<span name="2.3.295">their brains! that we should, with joy, pleasance</span><br>
<span name="2.3.296">revel and applause, transform ourselves into beasts!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.297">Why, but you are now well enough: how came you thus</span><br>
<span name="2.3.298">recovered?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.299">It hath pleased the devil drunkenness to give place</span><br>
<span name="2.3.300">to the devil wrath; one unperfectness shows me</span><br>
<span name="2.3.301">another, to make me frankly despise myself.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.302">Come, you are too severe a moraler: as the time,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.303">the place, and the condition of this country</span><br>
<span name="2.3.304">stands, I could heartily wish this had not befallen;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.305">but, since it is as it is, mend it for your own good.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.306">I will ask him for my place again; he shall tell me</span><br>
<span name="2.3.307">I am a drunkard! Had I as many mouths as Hydra,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.308">such an answer would stop them all. To be now a</span><br>
<span name="2.3.309">sensible man, by and by a fool, and presently a</span><br>
<span name="2.3.310">beast! O strange! Every inordinate cup is</span><br>
<span name="2.3.311">unblessed and the ingredient is a devil.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.312">Come, come, good wine is a good familiar creature,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.313">if it be well used: exclaim no more against it.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.314">And, good lieutenant, I think you think I love you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.315">I have well approved it, sir. I drunk!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.316">You or any man living may be drunk! at a time, man.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.317">I'll tell you what you shall do. Our general's wife</span><br>
<span name="2.3.318">is now the general: may say so in this respect, for</span><br>
<span name="2.3.319">that he hath devoted and given up himself to the</span><br>
<span name="2.3.320">contemplation, mark, and denotement of her parts and</span><br>
<span name="2.3.321">graces: confess yourself freely to her; importune</span><br>
<span name="2.3.322">her help to put you in your place again: she is of</span><br>
<span name="2.3.323">so free, so kind, so apt, so blessed a disposition,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.324">she holds it a vice in her goodness not to do more</span><br>
<span name="2.3.325">than she is requested: this broken joint between</span><br>
<span name="2.3.326">you and her husband entreat her to splinter; and, my</span><br>
<span name="2.3.327">fortunes against any lay worth naming, this</span><br>
<span name="2.3.328">crack of your love shall grow stronger than it was before.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.329">You advise me well.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.330">I protest, in the sincerity of love and honest kindness.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.331">I think it freely; and betimes in the morning I will</span><br>
<span name="2.3.332">beseech the virtuous Desdemona to undertake for me:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.333">I am desperate of my fortunes if they cheque me here.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.334">You are in the right. Good night, lieutenant; I</span><br>
<span name="2.3.335">must to the watch.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.336">CASSIO: Good night, honest Iago.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.337">And what's he then that says I play the villain?</span><br>
<span name="2.3.338">When this advice is free I give and honest,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.339">Probal to thinking and indeed the course</span><br>
<span name="2.3.340">To win the Moor again? For 'tis most easy</span><br>
<span name="2.3.341">The inclining Desdemona to subdue</span><br>
<span name="2.3.342">In any honest suit: she's framed as fruitful</span><br>
<span name="2.3.343">As the free elements. And then for her</span><br>
<span name="2.3.344">To win the Moor--were't to renounce his baptism,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.345">All seals and symbols of redeemed sin,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.346">His soul is so enfetter'd to her love,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.347">That she may make, unmake, do what she list,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.348">Even as her appetite shall play the god</span><br>
<span name="2.3.349">With his weak function. How am I then a villain</span><br>
<span name="2.3.350">To counsel Cassio to this parallel course,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.351">Directly to his good? Divinity of hell!</span><br>
<span name="2.3.352">When devils will the blackest sins put on,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.353">They do suggest at first with heavenly shows,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.354">As I do now: for whiles this honest fool</span><br>
<span name="2.3.355">Plies Desdemona to repair his fortunes</span><br>
<span name="2.3.356">And she for him pleads strongly to the Moor,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.357">I'll pour this pestilence into his ear,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.358">That she repeals him for her body's lust;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.359">And by how much she strives to do him good,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.360">She shall undo her credit with the Moor.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.361">So will I turn her virtue into pitch,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.362">And out of her own goodness make the net</span><br>
<span name="2.3.363">That shall enmesh them all.</span><br>
<p><i>Re-enter RODERIGO</i></p>
<span name="2.3.364">How now, Roderigo!</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.365">I do follow here in the chase, not like a hound that</span><br>
<span name="2.3.366">hunts, but one that fills up the cry. My money is</span><br>
<span name="2.3.367">almost spent; I have been to-night exceedingly well</span><br>
<span name="2.3.368">cudgelled; and I think the issue will be, I shall</span><br>
<span name="2.3.369">have so much experience for my pains, and so, with</span><br>
<span name="2.3.370">no money at all and a little more wit, return again to Venice.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="2.3.371">How poor are they that have not patience!</span><br>
<span name="2.3.372">What wound did ever heal but by degrees?</span><br>
<span name="2.3.373">Thou know'st we work by wit, and not by witchcraft;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.374">And wit depends on dilatory time.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.375">Does't not go well? Cassio hath beaten thee.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.376">And thou, by that small hurt, hast cashier'd Cassio:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.377">Though other things grow fair against the sun,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.378">Yet fruits that blossom first will first be ripe:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.379">Content thyself awhile. By the mass, 'tis morning;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.380">Pleasure and action make the hours seem short.</span><br>
<span name="2.3.381">Retire thee; go where thou art billeted:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.382">Away, I say; thou shalt know more hereafter:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.383">Nay, get thee gone.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit RODERIGO</i></p>
<span name="2.3.384">Two things are to be done:</span><br>
<span name="2.3.385">My wife must move for Cassio to her mistress;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.386">I'll set her on;</span><br>
<span name="2.3.387">Myself the while to draw the Moor apart,</span><br>
<span name="2.3.388">And bring him jump when he may Cassio find</span><br>
<span name="2.3.389">Soliciting his wife: ay, that's the way</span><br>
<span name="2.3.390">Dull not device by coldness and delay.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<br><p>
</p><h3>ACT III</h3>
<h3>SCENE I. Before the castle.</h3>
<p></p><br>
<i>Enter CASSIO and some Musicians</i>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.1">Masters, play here; I will content your pains;</span><br>
<span name="3.1.2">Something that's brief; and bid 'Good morrow, general.'</span><br>
<p><i>Music</i></p>
<p><i>Enter Clown</i></p>
<br>

<b>Clown</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.3">Why masters, have your instruments been in Naples,</span><br>
<span name="3.1.4">that they speak i' the nose thus?</span><br>
<br>

<b>First Musician</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.5">How, sir, how!</span><br>
<br>

<b>Clown</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.6">Are these, I pray you, wind-instruments?</span><br>
<br>

<b>First Musician</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.7">Ay, marry, are they, sir.</span><br>
<br>

<b>Clown</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.8">O, thereby hangs a tail.</span><br>
<br>

<b>First Musician</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.9">Whereby hangs a tale, sir?</span><br>
<br>

<b>Clown</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.10">Marry. sir, by many a wind-instrument that I know.</span><br>
<span name="3.1.11">But, masters, here's money for you: and the general</span><br>
<span name="3.1.12">so likes your music, that he desires you, for love's</span><br>
<span name="3.1.13">sake, to make no more noise with it.</span><br>
<br>

<b>First Musician</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.14">Well, sir, we will not.</span><br>
<br>

<b>Clown</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.15">If you have any music that may not be heard, to't</span><br>
<span name="3.1.16">again: but, as they say to hear music the general</span><br>
<span name="3.1.17">does not greatly care.</span><br>
<br>

<b>First Musician</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.18">We have none such, sir.</span><br>
<br>

<b>Clown</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.19">Then put up your pipes in your bag, for I'll away:</span><br>
<span name="3.1.20">go; vanish into air; away!</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt Musicians</i></p>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.21">Dost thou hear, my honest friend?</span><br>
<br>

<b>Clown</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.22">No, I hear not your honest friend; I hear you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.23">Prithee, keep up thy quillets. There's a poor piece</span><br>
<span name="3.1.24">of gold for thee: if the gentlewoman that attends</span><br>
<span name="3.1.25">the general's wife be stirring, tell her there's</span><br>
<span name="3.1.26">one Cassio entreats her a little favour of speech:</span><br>
<span name="3.1.27">wilt thou do this?</span><br>
<br>

<b>Clown</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.28">She is stirring, sir: if she will stir hither, I</span><br>
<span name="3.1.29">shall seem to notify unto her.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.30">Do, good my friend.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit Clown</i></p>
<p><i>Enter IAGO</i></p>
<span name="3.1.31">In happy time, Iago.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.32">You have not been a-bed, then?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.33">Why, no; the day had broke</span><br>
<span name="3.1.34">Before we parted. I have made bold, Iago,</span><br>
<span name="3.1.35">To send in to your wife: my suit to her</span><br>
<span name="3.1.36">Is, that she will to virtuous Desdemona</span><br>
<span name="3.1.37">Procure me some access.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.38">I'll send her to you presently;</span><br>
<span name="3.1.39">And I'll devise a mean to draw the Moor</span><br>
<span name="3.1.40">Out of the way, that your converse and business</span><br>
<span name="3.1.41">May be more free.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.42">I humbly thank you for't.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit IAGO</i></p>
<span name="3.1.43">I never knew</span><br>
<span name="3.1.44">A Florentine more kind and honest.</span><br>
<p><i>Enter EMILIA</i></p>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.45">Good morrow, good Lieutenant: I am sorry</span><br>
<span name="3.1.46">For your displeasure; but all will sure be well.</span><br>
<span name="3.1.47">The general and his wife are talking of it;</span><br>
<span name="3.1.48">And she speaks for you stoutly: the Moor replies,</span><br>
<span name="3.1.49">That he you hurt is of great fame in Cyprus,</span><br>
<span name="3.1.50">And great affinity, and that in wholesome wisdom</span><br>
<span name="3.1.51">He might not but refuse you; but he protests he loves you</span><br>
<span name="3.1.52">And needs no other suitor but his likings</span><br>
<span name="3.1.53">To take the safest occasion by the front</span><br>
<span name="3.1.54">To bring you in again.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.55">Yet, I beseech you,</span><br>
<span name="3.1.56">If you think fit, or that it may be done,</span><br>
<span name="3.1.57">Give me advantage of some brief discourse</span><br>
<span name="3.1.58">With Desdemona alone.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.59">Pray you, come in;</span><br>
<span name="3.1.60">I will bestow you where you shall have time</span><br>
<span name="3.1.61">To speak your bosom freely.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.1.62">I am much bound to you.</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
<br>
<h3>SCENE II. A room in the castle.</h3>
<p></p><br>
<i>Enter OTHELLO, IAGO, and Gentlemen</i>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.2.1">These letters give, Iago, to the pilot;</span><br>
<span name="3.2.2">And by him do my duties to the senate:</span><br>
<span name="3.2.3">That done, I will be walking on the works;</span><br>
<span name="3.2.4">Repair there to me.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.2.5">Well, my good lord, I'll do't.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.2.6">This fortification, gentlemen, shall we see't?</span><br>
<br>

<b>Gentleman</b>
<br>
<span name="3.2.7">We'll wait upon your lordship.</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
<br>
<h3>SCENE III. The garden of the castle.</h3>
<p></p><br>
<i>Enter DESDEMONA, CASSIO, and EMILIA</i>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.1">Be thou assured, good Cassio, I will do</span><br>
<span name="3.3.2">All my abilities in thy behalf.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.3">Good madam, do: I warrant it grieves my husband,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.4">As if the case were his.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.5">O, that's an honest fellow. Do not doubt, Cassio,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.6">But I will have my lord and you again</span><br>
<span name="3.3.7">As friendly as you were.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.8">Bounteous madam,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.9">Whatever shall become of Michael Cassio,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.10">He's never any thing but your true servant.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.11">I know't; I thank you. You do love my lord:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.12">You have known him long; and be you well assured</span><br>
<span name="3.3.13">He shall in strangeness stand no further off</span><br>
<span name="3.3.14">Than in a polite distance.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.15">Ay, but, lady,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.16">That policy may either last so long,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.17">Or feed upon such nice and waterish diet,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.18">Or breed itself so out of circumstance,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.19">That, I being absent and my place supplied,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.20">My general will forget my love and service.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.21">Do not doubt that; before Emilia here</span><br>
<span name="3.3.22">I give thee warrant of thy place: assure thee,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.23">If I do vow a friendship, I'll perform it</span><br>
<span name="3.3.24">To the last article: my lord shall never rest;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.25">I'll watch him tame and talk him out of patience;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.26">His bed shall seem a school, his board a shrift;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.27">I'll intermingle every thing he does</span><br>
<span name="3.3.28">With Cassio's suit: therefore be merry, Cassio;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.29">For thy solicitor shall rather die</span><br>
<span name="3.3.30">Than give thy cause away.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.31">Madam, here comes my lord.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.32">Madam, I'll take my leave.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.33">Why, stay, and hear me speak.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.34">Madam, not now: I am very ill at ease,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.35">Unfit for mine own purposes.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.36">Well, do your discretion.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit CASSIO</i></p>
<p><i>Enter OTHELLO and IAGO</i></p>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.37">Ha! I like not that.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.38">What dost thou say?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.39">Nothing, my lord: or if--I know not what.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.40">Was not that Cassio parted from my wife?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.41">Cassio, my lord! No, sure, I cannot think it,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.42">That he would steal away so guilty-like,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.43">Seeing you coming.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.44">                  I do believe 'twas he.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.45">How now, my lord!</span><br>
<span name="3.3.46">I have been talking with a suitor here,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.47">A man that languishes in your displeasure.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.48">Who is't you mean?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.49">Why, your lieutenant, Cassio. Good my lord,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.50">If I have any grace or power to move you,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.51">His present reconciliation take;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.52">For if he be not one that truly loves you,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.53">That errs in ignorance and not in cunning,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.54">I have no judgment in an honest face:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.55">I prithee, call him back.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.56">Went he hence now?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.57">Ay, sooth; so humbled</span><br>
<span name="3.3.58">That he hath left part of his grief with me,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.59">To suffer with him. Good love, call him back.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.60">Not now, sweet Desdemona; some other time.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.61">But shall't be shortly?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.62">The sooner, sweet, for you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.63">Shall't be to-night at supper?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.64">No, not to-night.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.65">To-morrow dinner, then?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.66">I shall not dine at home;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.67">I meet the captains at the citadel.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.68">Why, then, to-morrow night; or Tuesday morn;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.69">On Tuesday noon, or night; on Wednesday morn:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.70">I prithee, name the time, but let it not</span><br>
<span name="3.3.71">Exceed three days: in faith, he's penitent;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.72">And yet his trespass, in our common reason--</span><br>
<span name="3.3.73">Save that, they say, the wars must make examples</span><br>
<span name="3.3.74">Out of their best--is not almost a fault</span><br>
<span name="3.3.75">To incur a private cheque. When shall he come?</span><br>
<span name="3.3.76">Tell me, Othello: I wonder in my soul,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.77">What you would ask me, that I should deny,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.78">Or stand so mammering on. What! Michael Cassio,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.79">That came a-wooing with you, and so many a time,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.80">When I have spoke of you dispraisingly,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.81">Hath ta'en your part; to have so much to do</span><br>
<span name="3.3.82">To bring him in! Trust me, I could do much,--</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.83">Prithee, no more: let him come when he will;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.84">I will deny thee nothing.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.85">Why, this is not a boon;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.86">'Tis as I should entreat you wear your gloves,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.87">Or feed on nourishing dishes, or keep you warm,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.88">Or sue to you to do a peculiar profit</span><br>
<span name="3.3.89">To your own person: nay, when I have a suit</span><br>
<span name="3.3.90">Wherein I mean to touch your love indeed,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.91">It shall be full of poise and difficult weight</span><br>
<span name="3.3.92">And fearful to be granted.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.93">I will deny thee nothing:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.94">Whereon, I do beseech thee, grant me this,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.95">To leave me but a little to myself.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.96">Shall I deny you? no: farewell, my lord.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.97">Farewell, my Desdemona: I'll come to thee straight.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.98">Emilia, come. Be as your fancies teach you;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.99">Whate'er you be, I am obedient.</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt DESDEMONA and EMILIA</i></p>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.100">Excellent wretch! Perdition catch my soul,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.101">But I do love thee! and when I love thee not,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.102">Chaos is come again.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.103">My noble lord--</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.104">                  What dost thou say, Iago?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.105">Did Michael Cassio, when you woo'd my lady,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.106">Know of your love?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.107">He did, from first to last: why dost thou ask?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.108">But for a satisfaction of my thought;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.109">No further harm.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.110">                  Why of thy thought, Iago?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.111">I did not think he had been acquainted with her.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.112">O, yes; and went between us very oft.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.113">Indeed!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.114">Indeed! ay, indeed: discern'st thou aught in that?</span><br>
<span name="3.3.115">Is he not honest?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.116">Honest, my lord!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.117">                  Honest! ay, honest.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.118">My lord, for aught I know.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.119">What dost thou think?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.120">Think, my lord!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.121">Think, my lord!</span><br>
<span name="3.3.122">By heaven, he echoes me,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.123">As if there were some monster in his thought</span><br>
<span name="3.3.124">Too hideous to be shown. Thou dost mean something:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.125">I heard thee say even now, thou likedst not that,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.126">When Cassio left my wife: what didst not like?</span><br>
<span name="3.3.127">And when I told thee he was of my counsel</span><br>
<span name="3.3.128">In my whole course of wooing, thou criedst 'Indeed!'</span><br>
<span name="3.3.129">And didst contract and purse thy brow together,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.130">As if thou then hadst shut up in thy brain</span><br>
<span name="3.3.131">Some horrible conceit: if thou dost love me,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.132">Show me thy thought.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.133">My lord, you know I love you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.134">I think thou dost;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.135">And, for I know thou'rt full of love and honesty,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.136">And weigh'st thy words before thou givest them breath,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.137">Therefore these stops of thine fright me the more:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.138">For such things in a false disloyal knave</span><br>
<span name="3.3.139">Are tricks of custom, but in a man that's just</span><br>
<span name="3.3.140">They are close delations, working from the heart</span><br>
<span name="3.3.141">That passion cannot rule.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.142">For Michael Cassio,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.143">I dare be sworn I think that he is honest.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.144">I think so too.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.145">                  Men should be what they seem;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.146">Or those that be not, would they might seem none!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.147">Certain, men should be what they seem.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.148">Why, then, I think Cassio's an honest man.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.149">Nay, yet there's more in this:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.150">I prithee, speak to me as to thy thinkings,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.151">As thou dost ruminate, and give thy worst of thoughts</span><br>
<span name="3.3.152">The worst of words.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.153">Good my lord, pardon me:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.154">Though I am bound to every act of duty,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.155">I am not bound to that all slaves are free to.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.156">Utter my thoughts? Why, say they are vile and false;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.157">As where's that palace whereinto foul things</span><br>
<span name="3.3.158">Sometimes intrude not? who has a breast so pure,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.159">But some uncleanly apprehensions</span><br>
<span name="3.3.160">Keep leets and law-days and in session sit</span><br>
<span name="3.3.161">With meditations lawful?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.162">Thou dost conspire against thy friend, Iago,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.163">If thou but think'st him wrong'd and makest his ear</span><br>
<span name="3.3.164">A stranger to thy thoughts.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.165">I do beseech you--</span><br>
<span name="3.3.166">Though I perchance am vicious in my guess,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.167">As, I confess, it is my nature's plague</span><br>
<span name="3.3.168">To spy into abuses, and oft my jealousy</span><br>
<span name="3.3.169">Shapes faults that are not--that your wisdom yet,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.170">From one that so imperfectly conceits,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.171">Would take no notice, nor build yourself a trouble</span><br>
<span name="3.3.172">Out of his scattering and unsure observance.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.173">It were not for your quiet nor your good,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.174">Nor for my manhood, honesty, or wisdom,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.175">To let you know my thoughts.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.176">What dost thou mean?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.177">Good name in man and woman, dear my lord,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.178">Is the immediate jewel of their souls:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.179">Who steals my purse steals trash; 'tis something, nothing;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.180">'Twas mine, 'tis his, and has been slave to thousands:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.181">But he that filches from me my good name</span><br>
<span name="3.3.182">Robs me of that which not enriches him</span><br>
<span name="3.3.183">And makes me poor indeed.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.184">By heaven, I'll know thy thoughts.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.185">You cannot, if my heart were in your hand;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.186">Nor shall not, whilst 'tis in my custody.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.187">Ha!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.188">O, beware, my lord, of jealousy;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.189">It is the green-eyed monster which doth mock</span><br>
<span name="3.3.190">The meat it feeds on; that cuckold lives in bliss</span><br>
<span name="3.3.191">Who, certain of his fate, loves not his wronger;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.192">But, O, what damned minutes tells he o'er</span><br>
<span name="3.3.193">Who dotes, yet doubts, suspects, yet strongly loves!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.194">O misery!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.195">Poor and content is rich and rich enough,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.196">But riches fineless is as poor as winter</span><br>
<span name="3.3.197">To him that ever fears he shall be poor.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.198">Good heaven, the souls of all my tribe defend</span><br>
<span name="3.3.199">From jealousy!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.200">                  Why, why is this?</span><br>
<span name="3.3.201">Think'st thou I'ld make a lie of jealousy,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.202">To follow still the changes of the moon</span><br>
<span name="3.3.203">With fresh suspicions? No; to be once in doubt</span><br>
<span name="3.3.204">Is once to be resolved: exchange me for a goat,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.205">When I shall turn the business of my soul</span><br>
<span name="3.3.206">To such exsufflicate and blown surmises,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.207">Matching thy inference. 'Tis not to make me jealous</span><br>
<span name="3.3.208">To say my wife is fair, feeds well, loves company,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.209">Is free of speech, sings, plays and dances well;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.210">Where virtue is, these are more virtuous:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.211">Nor from mine own weak merits will I draw</span><br>
<span name="3.3.212">The smallest fear or doubt of her revolt;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.213">For she had eyes, and chose me. No, Iago;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.214">I'll see before I doubt; when I doubt, prove;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.215">And on the proof, there is no more but this,--</span><br>
<span name="3.3.216">Away at once with love or jealousy!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.217">I am glad of it; for now I shall have reason</span><br>
<span name="3.3.218">To show the love and duty that I bear you</span><br>
<span name="3.3.219">With franker spirit: therefore, as I am bound,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.220">Receive it from me. I speak not yet of proof.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.221">Look to your wife; observe her well with Cassio;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.222">Wear your eye thus, not jealous nor secure:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.223">I would not have your free and noble nature,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.224">Out of self-bounty, be abused; look to't:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.225">I know our country disposition well;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.226">In Venice they do let heaven see the pranks</span><br>
<span name="3.3.227">They dare not show their husbands; their best conscience</span><br>
<span name="3.3.228">Is not to leave't undone, but keep't unknown.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.229">Dost thou say so?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.230">She did deceive her father, marrying you;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.231">And when she seem'd to shake and fear your looks,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.232">She loved them most.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.233">And so she did.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.234">Why, go to then;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.235">She that, so young, could give out such a seeming,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.236">To seal her father's eyes up close as oak-</span><br>
<span name="3.3.237">He thought 'twas witchcraft--but I am much to blame;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.238">I humbly do beseech you of your pardon</span><br>
<span name="3.3.239">For too much loving you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.240">I am bound to thee for ever.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.241">I see this hath a little dash'd your spirits.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.242">Not a jot, not a jot.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.243">I' faith, I fear it has.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.244">I hope you will consider what is spoke</span><br>
<span name="3.3.245">Comes from my love. But I do see you're moved:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.246">I am to pray you not to strain my speech</span><br>
<span name="3.3.247">To grosser issues nor to larger reach</span><br>
<span name="3.3.248">Than to suspicion.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.249">I will not.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.250">          Should you do so, my lord,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.251">My speech should fall into such vile success</span><br>
<span name="3.3.252">As my thoughts aim not at. Cassio's my worthy friend--</span><br>
<span name="3.3.253">My lord, I see you're moved.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.254">No, not much moved:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.255">I do not think but Desdemona's honest.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.256">Long live she so! and long live you to think so!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.257">And yet, how nature erring from itself,--</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.258">Ay, there's the point: as--to be bold with you--</span><br>
<span name="3.3.259">Not to affect many proposed matches</span><br>
<span name="3.3.260">Of her own clime, complexion, and degree,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.261">Whereto we see in all things nature tends--</span><br>
<span name="3.3.262">Foh! one may smell in such a will most rank,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.263">Foul disproportion thoughts unnatural.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.264">But pardon me; I do not in position</span><br>
<span name="3.3.265">Distinctly speak of her; though I may fear</span><br>
<span name="3.3.266">Her will, recoiling to her better judgment,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.267">May fall to match you with her country forms</span><br>
<span name="3.3.268">And happily repent.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.269">Farewell, farewell:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.270">If more thou dost perceive, let me know more;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.271">Set on thy wife to observe: leave me, Iago:</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.272">[Going]  My lord, I take my leave.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.273">Why did I marry? This honest creature doubtless</span><br>
<span name="3.3.274">Sees and knows more, much more, than he unfolds.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.275">[Returning]  My lord, I would I might entreat</span><br>
<span name="3.3.276">your honour</span><br>
<span name="3.3.277">To scan this thing no further; leave it to time:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.278">Though it be fit that Cassio have his place,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.279">For sure, he fills it up with great ability,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.280">Yet, if you please to hold him off awhile,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.281">You shall by that perceive him and his means:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.282">Note, if your lady strain his entertainment</span><br>
<span name="3.3.283">With any strong or vehement importunity;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.284">Much will be seen in that. In the mean time,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.285">Let me be thought too busy in my fears--</span><br>
<span name="3.3.286">As worthy cause I have to fear I am--</span><br>
<span name="3.3.287">And hold her free, I do beseech your honour.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.288">Fear not my government.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.289">I once more take my leave.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.290">This fellow's of exceeding honesty,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.291">And knows all qualities, with a learned spirit,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.292">Of human dealings. If I do prove her haggard,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.293">Though that her jesses were my dear heartstrings,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.294">I'ld whistle her off and let her down the wind,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.295">To pray at fortune. Haply, for I am black</span><br>
<span name="3.3.296">And have not those soft parts of conversation</span><br>
<span name="3.3.297">That chamberers have, or for I am declined</span><br>
<span name="3.3.298">Into the vale of years,--yet that's not much--</span><br>
<span name="3.3.299">She's gone. I am abused; and my relief</span><br>
<span name="3.3.300">Must be to loathe her. O curse of marriage,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.301">That we can call these delicate creatures ours,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.302">And not their appetites! I had rather be a toad,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.303">And live upon the vapour of a dungeon,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.304">Than keep a corner in the thing I love</span><br>
<span name="3.3.305">For others' uses. Yet, 'tis the plague of great ones;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.306">Prerogatived are they less than the base;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.307">'Tis destiny unshunnable, like death:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.308">Even then this forked plague is fated to us</span><br>
<span name="3.3.309">When we do quicken. Desdemona comes:</span><br>
<p><i>Re-enter DESDEMONA and EMILIA</i></p>
<span name="3.3.310">If she be false, O, then heaven mocks itself!</span><br>
<span name="3.3.311">I'll not believe't.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.312">How now, my dear Othello!</span><br>
<span name="3.3.313">Your dinner, and the generous islanders</span><br>
<span name="3.3.314">By you invited, do attend your presence.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.315">I am to blame.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.316">                  Why do you speak so faintly?</span><br>
<span name="3.3.317">Are you not well?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.318">I have a pain upon my forehead here.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.319">'Faith, that's with watching; 'twill away again:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.320">Let me but bind it hard, within this hour</span><br>
<span name="3.3.321">It will be well.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.322">                  Your napkin is too little:</span><br>
<p><i>He puts the handkerchief from him; and it drops</i></p>
<span name="3.3.323">Let it alone. Come, I'll go in with you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.324">I am very sorry that you are not well.</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt OTHELLO and DESDEMONA</i></p>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.325">I am glad I have found this napkin:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.326">This was her first remembrance from the Moor:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.327">My wayward husband hath a hundred times</span><br>
<span name="3.3.328">Woo'd me to steal it; but she so loves the token,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.329">For he conjured her she should ever keep it,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.330">That she reserves it evermore about her</span><br>
<span name="3.3.331">To kiss and talk to. I'll have the work ta'en out,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.332">And give't Iago: what he will do with it</span><br>
<span name="3.3.333">Heaven knows, not I;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.334">I nothing but to please his fantasy.</span><br>
<p><i>Re-enter Iago</i></p>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.335">How now! what do you here alone?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.336">Do not you chide; I have a thing for you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.337">A thing for me? it is a common thing--</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.338">Ha!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.339">To have a foolish wife.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.340">O, is that all? What will you give me now</span><br>
<span name="3.3.341">For the same handkerchief?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.342">What handkerchief?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.343">What handkerchief?</span><br>
<span name="3.3.344">Why, that the Moor first gave to Desdemona;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.345">That which so often you did bid me steal.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.346">Hast stol'n it from her?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.347">No, 'faith; she let it drop by negligence.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.348">And, to the advantage, I, being here, took't up.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.349">Look, here it is.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.350">                  A good wench; give it me.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.351">What will you do with 't, that you have been</span><br>
<span name="3.3.352">so earnest</span><br>
<span name="3.3.353">To have me filch it?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.354">[Snatching it]  Why, what's that to you?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.355">If it be not for some purpose of import,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.356">Give't me again: poor lady, she'll run mad</span><br>
<span name="3.3.357">When she shall lack it.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.358">Be not acknown on 't; I have use for it.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.359">Go, leave me.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit EMILIA</i></p>
<span name="3.3.360">I will in Cassio's lodging lose this napkin,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.361">And let him find it. Trifles light as air</span><br>
<span name="3.3.362">Are to the jealous confirmations strong</span><br>
<span name="3.3.363">As proofs of holy writ: this may do something.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.364">The Moor already changes with my poison:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.365">Dangerous conceits are, in their natures, poisons.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.366">Which at the first are scarce found to distaste,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.367">But with a little act upon the blood.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.368">Burn like the mines of Sulphur. I did say so:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.369">Look, where he comes!</span><br>
<p><i>Re-enter OTHELLO</i></p>
<span name="3.3.370">Not poppy, nor mandragora,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.371">Nor all the drowsy syrups of the world,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.372">Shall ever medicine thee to that sweet sleep</span><br>
<span name="3.3.373">Which thou owedst yesterday.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.374">Ha! ha! false to me?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.375">Why, how now, general! no more of that.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.376">Avaunt! be gone! thou hast set me on the rack:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.377">I swear 'tis better to be much abused</span><br>
<span name="3.3.378">Than but to know't a little.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.379">How now, my lord!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.380">What sense had I of her stol'n hours of lust?</span><br>
<span name="3.3.381">I saw't not, thought it not, it harm'd not me:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.382">I slept the next night well, was free and merry;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.383">I found not Cassio's kisses on her lips:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.384">He that is robb'd, not wanting what is stol'n,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.385">Let him not know't, and he's not robb'd at all.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.386">I am sorry to hear this.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.387">I had been happy, if the general camp,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.388">Pioners and all, had tasted her sweet body,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.389">So I had nothing known. O, now, for ever</span><br>
<span name="3.3.390">Farewell the tranquil mind! farewell content!</span><br>
<span name="3.3.391">Farewell the plumed troop, and the big wars,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.392">That make ambition virtue! O, farewell!</span><br>
<span name="3.3.393">Farewell the neighing steed, and the shrill trump,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.394">The spirit-stirring drum, the ear-piercing fife,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.395">The royal banner, and all quality,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.396">Pride, pomp and circumstance of glorious war!</span><br>
<span name="3.3.397">And, O you mortal engines, whose rude throats</span><br>
<span name="3.3.398">The immortal Jove's dead clamours counterfeit,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.399">Farewell! Othello's occupation's gone!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.400">Is't possible, my lord?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.401">Villain, be sure thou prove my love a whore,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.402">Be sure of it; give me the ocular proof:</span><br>
