<span name="3.3.403">Or by the worth of man's eternal soul,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.404">Thou hadst been better have been born a dog</span><br>
<span name="3.3.405">Than answer my waked wrath!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.406">Is't come to this?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.407">Make me to see't; or, at the least, so prove it,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.408">That the probation bear no hinge nor loop</span><br>
<span name="3.3.409">To hang a doubt on; or woe upon thy life!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.410">My noble lord,--</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.411">If thou dost slander her and torture me,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.412">Never pray more; abandon all remorse;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.413">On horror's head horrors accumulate;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.414">Do deeds to make heaven weep, all earth amazed;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.415">For nothing canst thou to damnation add</span><br>
<span name="3.3.416">Greater than that.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.417">                  O grace! O heaven forgive me!</span><br>
<span name="3.3.418">Are you a man? have you a soul or sense?</span><br>
<span name="3.3.419">God be wi' you; take mine office. O wretched fool.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.420">That livest to make thine honesty a vice!</span><br>
<span name="3.3.421">O monstrous world! Take note, take note, O world,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.422">To be direct and honest is not safe.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.423">I thank you for this profit; and from hence</span><br>
<span name="3.3.424">I'll love no friend, sith love breeds such offence.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.425">Nay, stay: thou shouldst be honest.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.426">I should be wise, for honesty's a fool</span><br>
<span name="3.3.427">And loses that it works for.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.428">By the world,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.429">I think my wife be honest and think she is not;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.430">I think that thou art just and think thou art not.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.431">I'll have some proof. Her name, that was as fresh</span><br>
<span name="3.3.432">As Dian's visage, is now begrimed and black</span><br>
<span name="3.3.433">As mine own face. If there be cords, or knives,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.434">Poison, or fire, or suffocating streams,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.435">I'll not endure it. Would I were satisfied!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.436">I see, sir, you are eaten up with passion:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.437">I do repent me that I put it to you.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.438">You would be satisfied?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.439">Would! nay, I will.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.440">And may: but, how? how satisfied, my lord?</span><br>
<span name="3.3.441">Would you, the supervisor, grossly gape on--</span><br>
<span name="3.3.442">Behold her topp'd?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.443">                  Death and damnation! O!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.444">It were a tedious difficulty, I think,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.445">To bring them to that prospect: damn them then,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.446">If ever mortal eyes do see them bolster</span><br>
<span name="3.3.447">More than their own! What then? how then?</span><br>
<span name="3.3.448">What shall I say? Where's satisfaction?</span><br>
<span name="3.3.449">It is impossible you should see this,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.450">Were they as prime as goats, as hot as monkeys,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.451">As salt as wolves in pride, and fools as gross</span><br>
<span name="3.3.452">As ignorance made drunk. But yet, I say,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.453">If imputation and strong circumstances,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.454">Which lead directly to the door of truth,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.455">Will give you satisfaction, you may have't.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.456">Give me a living reason she's disloyal.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.457">I do not like the office:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.458">But, sith I am enter'd in this cause so far,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.459">Prick'd to't by foolish honesty and love,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.460">I will go on. I lay with Cassio lately;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.461">And, being troubled with a raging tooth,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.462">I could not sleep.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.463">There are a kind of men so loose of soul,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.464">That in their sleeps will mutter their affairs:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.465">One of this kind is Cassio:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.466">In sleep I heard him say 'Sweet Desdemona,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.467">Let us be wary, let us hide our loves;'</span><br>
<span name="3.3.468">And then, sir, would he gripe and wring my hand,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.469">Cry 'O sweet creature!' and then kiss me hard,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.470">As if he pluck'd up kisses by the roots</span><br>
<span name="3.3.471">That grew upon my lips: then laid his leg</span><br>
<span name="3.3.472">Over my thigh, and sigh'd, and kiss'd; and then</span><br>
<span name="3.3.473">Cried 'Cursed fate that gave thee to the Moor!'</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.474">O monstrous! monstrous!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.475">Nay, this was but his dream.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.476">But this denoted a foregone conclusion:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.477">'Tis a shrewd doubt, though it be but a dream.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.478">And this may help to thicken other proofs</span><br>
<span name="3.3.479">That do demonstrate thinly.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.480">I'll tear her all to pieces.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.481">Nay, but be wise: yet we see nothing done;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.482">She may be honest yet. Tell me but this,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.483">Have you not sometimes seen a handkerchief</span><br>
<span name="3.3.484">Spotted with strawberries in your wife's hand?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.485">I gave her such a one; 'twas my first gift.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.486">I know not that; but such a handkerchief--</span><br>
<span name="3.3.487">I am sure it was your wife's--did I to-day</span><br>
<span name="3.3.488">See Cassio wipe his beard with.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.489">If it be that--</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.490">If it be that, or any that was hers,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.491">It speaks against her with the other proofs.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.492">O, that the slave had forty thousand lives!</span><br>
<span name="3.3.493">One is too poor, too weak for my revenge.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.494">Now do I see 'tis true. Look here, Iago;</span><br>
<span name="3.3.495">All my fond love thus do I blow to heaven.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.496">'Tis gone.</span><br>
<span name="3.3.497">Arise, black vengeance, from thy hollow cell!</span><br>
<span name="3.3.498">Yield up, O love, thy crown and hearted throne</span><br>
<span name="3.3.499">To tyrannous hate! Swell, bosom, with thy fraught,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.500">For 'tis of aspics' tongues!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.501">Yet be content.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.502">O, blood, blood, blood!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.503">Patience, I say; your mind perhaps may change.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.504">Never, Iago: Like to the Pontic sea,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.505">Whose icy current and compulsive course</span><br>
<span name="3.3.506">Ne'er feels retiring ebb, but keeps due on</span><br>
<span name="3.3.507">To the Propontic and the Hellespont,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.508">Even so my bloody thoughts, with violent pace,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.509">Shall ne'er look back, ne'er ebb to humble love,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.510">Till that a capable and wide revenge</span><br>
<span name="3.3.511">Swallow them up. Now, by yond marble heaven,</span><br>
<p><i>Kneels</i></p>
<span name="3.3.512">In the due reverence of a sacred vow</span><br>
<span name="3.3.513">I here engage my words.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.514">Do not rise yet.</span><br>
<p><i>Kneels</i></p>
<span name="3.3.515">Witness, you ever-burning lights above,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.516">You elements that clip us round about,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.517">Witness that here Iago doth give up</span><br>
<span name="3.3.518">The execution of his wit, hands, heart,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.519">To wrong'd Othello's service! Let him command,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.520">And to obey shall be in me remorse,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.521">What bloody business ever.</span><br>
<p><i>They rise</i></p>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.522">I greet thy love,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.523">Not with vain thanks, but with acceptance bounteous,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.524">And will upon the instant put thee to't:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.525">Within these three days let me hear thee say</span><br>
<span name="3.3.526">That Cassio's not alive.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.527">My friend is dead; 'tis done at your request:</span><br>
<span name="3.3.528">But let her live.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.529">Damn her, lewd minx! O, damn her!</span><br>
<span name="3.3.530">Come, go with me apart; I will withdraw,</span><br>
<span name="3.3.531">To furnish me with some swift means of death</span><br>
<span name="3.3.532">For the fair devil. Now art thou my lieutenant.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.3.533">I am your own for ever.</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
<br>
<h3>SCENE IV. Before the castle.</h3>
<p></p><br>
<i>Enter DESDEMONA, EMILIA, and Clown</i>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.1">Do you know, sirrah, where Lieutenant Cassio lies?</span><br>
<br>

<b>Clown</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.2">I dare not say he lies any where.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.3">Why, man?</span><br>
<br>

<b>Clown</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.4">He's a soldier, and for one to say a soldier lies,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.5">is stabbing.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.6">Go to: where lodges he?</span><br>
<br>

<b>Clown</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.7">To tell you where he lodges, is to tell you where I lie.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.8">Can any thing be made of this?</span><br>
<br>

<b>Clown</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.9">I know not where he lodges, and for me to devise a</span><br>
<span name="3.4.10">lodging and say he lies here or he lies there, were</span><br>
<span name="3.4.11">to lie in mine own throat.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.12">Can you inquire him out, and be edified by report?</span><br>
<br>

<b>Clown</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.13">I will catechise the world for him; that is, make</span><br>
<span name="3.4.14">questions, and by them answer.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.15">Seek him, bid him come hither: tell him I have</span><br>
<span name="3.4.16">moved my lord on his behalf, and hope all will be well.</span><br>
<br>

<b>Clown</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.17">To do this is within the compass of man's wit: and</span><br>
<span name="3.4.18">therefore I will attempt the doing it.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.19">Where should I lose that handkerchief, Emilia?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.20">I know not, madam.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.21">Believe me, I had rather have lost my purse</span><br>
<span name="3.4.22">Full of crusadoes: and, but my noble Moor</span><br>
<span name="3.4.23">Is true of mind and made of no such baseness</span><br>
<span name="3.4.24">As jealous creatures are, it were enough</span><br>
<span name="3.4.25">To put him to ill thinking.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.26">Is he not jealous?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.27">Who, he? I think the sun where he was born</span><br>
<span name="3.4.28">Drew all such humours from him.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.29">Look, where he comes.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.30">I will not leave him now till Cassio</span><br>
<span name="3.4.31">Be call'd to him.</span><br>
<p><i>Enter OTHELLO</i></p>
<span name="3.4.32">How is't with you, my lord</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.33">Well, my good lady.</span><br>
<p><i>Aside</i></p>
<span name="3.4.34">O, hardness to dissemble!--</span><br>
<span name="3.4.35">How do you, Desdemona?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.36">Well, my good lord.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.37">Give me your hand: this hand is moist, my lady.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.38">It yet hath felt no age nor known no sorrow.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.39">This argues fruitfulness and liberal heart:</span><br>
<span name="3.4.40">Hot, hot, and moist: this hand of yours requires</span><br>
<span name="3.4.41">A sequester from liberty, fasting and prayer,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.42">Much castigation, exercise devout;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.43">For here's a young and sweating devil here,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.44">That commonly rebels. 'Tis a good hand,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.45">A frank one.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.46">                  You may, indeed, say so;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.47">For 'twas that hand that gave away my heart.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.48">A liberal hand: the hearts of old gave hands;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.49">But our new heraldry is hands, not hearts.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.50">I cannot speak of this. Come now, your promise.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.51">What promise, chuck?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.52">I have sent to bid Cassio come speak with you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.53">I have a salt and sorry rheum offends me;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.54">Lend me thy handkerchief.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.55">Here, my lord.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.56">That which I gave you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.57">I have it not about me.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.58">Not?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.59">   No, indeed, my lord.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.60">That is a fault.</span><br>
<span name="3.4.61">That handkerchief</span><br>
<span name="3.4.62">Did an Egyptian to my mother give;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.63">She was a charmer, and could almost read</span><br>
<span name="3.4.64">The thoughts of people: she told her, while</span><br>
<span name="3.4.65">she kept it,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.66">'Twould make her amiable and subdue my father</span><br>
<span name="3.4.67">Entirely to her love, but if she lost it</span><br>
<span name="3.4.68">Or made gift of it, my father's eye</span><br>
<span name="3.4.69">Should hold her loathed and his spirits should hunt</span><br>
<span name="3.4.70">After new fancies: she, dying, gave it me;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.71">And bid me, when my fate would have me wive,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.72">To give it her. I did so: and take heed on't;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.73">Make it a darling like your precious eye;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.74">To lose't or give't away were such perdition</span><br>
<span name="3.4.75">As nothing else could match.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.76">Is't possible?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.77">'Tis true: there's magic in the web of it:</span><br>
<span name="3.4.78">A sibyl, that had number'd in the world</span><br>
<span name="3.4.79">The sun to course two hundred compasses,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.80">In her prophetic fury sew'd the work;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.81">The worms were hallow'd that did breed the silk;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.82">And it was dyed in mummy which the skilful</span><br>
<span name="3.4.83">Conserved of maidens' hearts.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.84">Indeed! is't true?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.85">Most veritable; therefore look to't well.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.86">Then would to God that I had never seen't!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.87">Ha! wherefore?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.88">Why do you speak so startingly and rash?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.89">Is't lost? is't gone? speak, is it out</span><br>
<span name="3.4.90">o' the way?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.91">Heaven bless us!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.92">Say you?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.93">It is not lost; but what an if it were?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.94">How!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.95">I say, it is not lost.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.96">Fetch't, let me see't.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.97">Why, so I can, sir, but I will not now.</span><br>
<span name="3.4.98">This is a trick to put me from my suit:</span><br>
<span name="3.4.99">Pray you, let Cassio be received again.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.100">Fetch me the handkerchief: my mind misgives.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.101">Come, come;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.102">You'll never meet a more sufficient man.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.103">The handkerchief!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.104">                  I pray, talk me of Cassio.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.105">The handkerchief!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.106">                  A man that all his time</span><br>
<span name="3.4.107">Hath founded his good fortunes on your love,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.108">Shared dangers with you,--</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.109">The handkerchief!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.110">In sooth, you are to blame.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.111">Away!</span><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.112">Is not this man jealous?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.113">I ne'er saw this before.</span><br>
<span name="3.4.114">Sure, there's some wonder in this handkerchief:</span><br>
<span name="3.4.115">I am most unhappy in the loss of it.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.116">'Tis not a year or two shows us a man:</span><br>
<span name="3.4.117">They are all but stomachs, and we all but food;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.118">To eat us hungerly, and when they are full,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.119">They belch us. Look you, Cassio and my husband!</span><br>
<p><i>Enter CASSIO and IAGO</i></p>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.120">There is no other way; 'tis she must do't:</span><br>
<span name="3.4.121">And, lo, the happiness! go, and importune her.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.122">How now, good Cassio! what's the news with you?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.123">Madam, my former suit: I do beseech you</span><br>
<span name="3.4.124">That by your virtuous means I may again</span><br>
<span name="3.4.125">Exist, and be a member of his love</span><br>
<span name="3.4.126">Whom I with all the office of my heart</span><br>
<span name="3.4.127">Entirely honour: I would not be delay'd.</span><br>
<span name="3.4.128">If my offence be of such mortal kind</span><br>
<span name="3.4.129">That nor my service past, nor present sorrows,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.130">Nor purposed merit in futurity,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.131">Can ransom me into his love again,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.132">But to know so must be my benefit;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.133">So shall I clothe me in a forced content,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.134">And shut myself up in some other course,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.135">To fortune's alms.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.136">                  Alas, thrice-gentle Cassio!</span><br>
<span name="3.4.137">My advocation is not now in tune;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.138">My lord is not my lord; nor should I know him,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.139">Were he in favour as in humour alter'd.</span><br>
<span name="3.4.140">So help me every spirit sanctified,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.141">As I have spoken for you all my best</span><br>
<span name="3.4.142">And stood within the blank of his displeasure</span><br>
<span name="3.4.143">For my free speech! you must awhile be patient:</span><br>
<span name="3.4.144">What I can do I will; and more I will</span><br>
<span name="3.4.145">Than for myself I dare: let that suffice you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.146">Is my lord angry?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.147">                  He went hence but now,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.148">And certainly in strange unquietness.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.149">Can he be angry? I have seen the cannon,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.150">When it hath blown his ranks into the air,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.151">And, like the devil, from his very arm</span><br>
<span name="3.4.152">Puff'd his own brother:--and can he be angry?</span><br>
<span name="3.4.153">Something of moment then: I will go meet him:</span><br>
<span name="3.4.154">There's matter in't indeed, if he be angry.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.155">I prithee, do so.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit IAGO</i></p>
<span name="3.4.156">Something, sure, of state,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.157">Either from Venice, or some unhatch'd practise</span><br>
<span name="3.4.158">Made demonstrable here in Cyprus to him,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.159">Hath puddled his clear spirit: and in such cases</span><br>
<span name="3.4.160">Men's natures wrangle with inferior things,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.161">Though great ones are their object. 'Tis even so;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.162">For let our finger ache, and it indues</span><br>
<span name="3.4.163">Our other healthful members even to that sense</span><br>
<span name="3.4.164">Of pain: nay, we must think men are not gods,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.165">Nor of them look for such observances</span><br>
<span name="3.4.166">As fit the bridal. Beshrew me much, Emilia,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.167">I was, unhandsome warrior as I am,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.168">Arraigning his unkindness with my soul;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.169">But now I find I had suborn'd the witness,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.170">And he's indicted falsely.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.171">Pray heaven it be state-matters, as you think,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.172">And no conception nor no jealous toy</span><br>
<span name="3.4.173">Concerning you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.174">Alas the day! I never gave him cause.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.175">But jealous souls will not be answer'd so;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.176">They are not ever jealous for the cause,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.177">But jealous for they are jealous: 'tis a monster</span><br>
<span name="3.4.178">Begot upon itself, born on itself.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.179">Heaven keep that monster from Othello's mind!</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.180">Lady, amen.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.181">I will go seek him. Cassio, walk hereabout:</span><br>
<span name="3.4.182">If I do find him fit, I'll move your suit</span><br>
<span name="3.4.183">And seek to effect it to my uttermost.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.184">I humbly thank your ladyship.</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt DESDEMONA and EMILIA</i></p>
<p><i>Enter BIANCA</i></p>
<br>

<b>BIANCA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.185">Save you, friend Cassio!</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.186">What make you from home?</span><br>
<span name="3.4.187">How is it with you, my most fair Bianca?</span><br>
<span name="3.4.188">I' faith, sweet love, I was coming to your house.</span><br>
<br>

<b>BIANCA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.189">And I was going to your lodging, Cassio.</span><br>
<span name="3.4.190">What, keep a week away? seven days and nights?</span><br>
<span name="3.4.191">Eight score eight hours? and lovers' absent hours,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.192">More tedious than the dial eight score times?</span><br>
<span name="3.4.193">O weary reckoning!</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.194">                  Pardon me, Bianca:</span><br>
<span name="3.4.195">I have this while with leaden thoughts been press'd:</span><br>
<span name="3.4.196">But I shall, in a more continuate time,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.197">Strike off this score of absence. Sweet Bianca,</span><br>
<p><i>Giving her DESDEMONA's handkerchief</i></p>
<span name="3.4.198">Take me this work out.</span><br>
<br>

<b>BIANCA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.199">O Cassio, whence came this?</span><br>
<span name="3.4.200">This is some token from a newer friend:</span><br>
<span name="3.4.201">To the felt absence now I feel a cause:</span><br>
<span name="3.4.202">Is't come to this? Well, well.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.203">Go to, woman!</span><br>
<span name="3.4.204">Throw your vile guesses in the devil's teeth,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.205">From whence you have them. You are jealous now</span><br>
<span name="3.4.206">That this is from some mistress, some remembrance:</span><br>
<span name="3.4.207">No, in good troth, Bianca.</span><br>
<br>

<b>BIANCA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.208">Why, whose is it?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.209">I know not, sweet: I found it in my chamber.</span><br>
<span name="3.4.210">I like the work well: ere it be demanded--</span><br>
<span name="3.4.211">As like enough it will--I'ld have it copied:</span><br>
<span name="3.4.212">Take it, and do't; and leave me for this time.</span><br>
<br>

<b>BIANCA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.213">Leave you! wherefore?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.214">I do attend here on the general;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.215">And think it no addition, nor my wish,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.216">To have him see me woman'd.</span><br>
<br>

<b>BIANCA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.217">Why, I pray you?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.218">Not that I love you not.</span><br>
<br>

<b>BIANCA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.219">But that you do not love me.</span><br>
<span name="3.4.220">I pray you, bring me on the way a little,</span><br>
<span name="3.4.221">And say if I shall see you soon at night.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.222">'Tis but a little way that I can bring you;</span><br>
<span name="3.4.223">For I attend here: but I'll see you soon.</span><br>
<br>

<b>BIANCA</b>
<br>
<span name="3.4.224">'Tis very good; I must be circumstanced.</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
<br><p>
</p><h3>ACT IV</h3>
<h3>SCENE I. Cyprus. Before the castle.</h3>
<p></p><br>
<i>Enter OTHELLO and IAGO</i>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.1">Will you think so?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.2">                  Think so, Iago!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.3">What,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.4">To kiss in private?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.5">An unauthorized kiss.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.6">Or to be naked with her friend in bed</span><br>
<span name="4.1.7">An hour or more, not meaning any harm?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.8">Naked in bed, Iago, and not mean harm!</span><br>
<span name="4.1.9">It is hypocrisy against the devil:</span><br>
<span name="4.1.10">They that mean virtuously, and yet do so,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.11">The devil their virtue tempts, and they tempt heaven.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.12">So they do nothing, 'tis a venial slip:</span><br>
<span name="4.1.13">But if I give my wife a handkerchief,--</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.14">What then?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.15">Why, then, 'tis hers, my lord; and, being hers,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.16">She may, I think, bestow't on any man.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.17">She is protectress of her honour too:</span><br>
<span name="4.1.18">May she give that?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.19">Her honour is an essence that's not seen;</span><br>
<span name="4.1.20">They have it very oft that have it not:</span><br>
<span name="4.1.21">But, for the handkerchief,--</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.22">By heaven, I would most gladly have forgot it.</span><br>
<span name="4.1.23">Thou said'st, it comes o'er my memory,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.24">As doth the raven o'er the infected house,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.25">Boding to all--he had my handkerchief.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.26">Ay, what of that?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.27">                  That's not so good now.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.28">What,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.29">If I had said I had seen him do you wrong?</span><br>
<span name="4.1.30">Or heard him say,--as knaves be such abroad,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.31">Who having, by their own importunate suit,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.32">Or voluntary dotage of some mistress,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.33">Convinced or supplied them, cannot choose</span><br>
<span name="4.1.34">But they must blab--</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.35">Hath he said any thing?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.36">He hath, my lord; but be you well assured,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.37">No more than he'll unswear.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.38">What hath he said?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.39">'Faith, that he did--I know not what he did.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.40">What? what?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.41">Lie--</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.42">    With her?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.43">With her, on her; what you will.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.44">Lie with her! lie on her! We say lie on her, when</span><br>
<span name="4.1.45">they belie her. Lie with her! that's fulsome.</span><br>
<span name="4.1.46">--Handkerchief--confessions--handkerchief!--To</span><br>
<span name="4.1.47">confess, and be hanged for his labour;--first, to be</span><br>
<span name="4.1.48">hanged, and then to confess.--I tremble at it.</span><br>
<span name="4.1.49">Nature would not invest herself in such shadowing</span><br>
<span name="4.1.50">passion without some instruction. It is not words</span><br>
<span name="4.1.51">that shake me thus. Pish! Noses, ears, and lips.</span><br>
<span name="4.1.52">--Is't possible?--Confess--handkerchief!--O devil!--</span><br>
<p><i>Falls in a trance</i></p>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.53">Work on,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.54">My medicine, work! Thus credulous fools are caught;</span><br>
<span name="4.1.55">And many worthy and chaste dames even thus,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.56">All guiltless, meet reproach. What, ho! my lord!</span><br>
<span name="4.1.57">My lord, I say! Othello!</span><br>
<p><i>Enter CASSIO</i></p>
<span name="4.1.58">How now, Cassio!</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.59">What's the matter?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.60">My lord is fall'n into an epilepsy:</span><br>
<span name="4.1.61">This is his second fit; he had one yesterday.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.62">Rub him about the temples.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.63">No, forbear;</span><br>
<span name="4.1.64">The lethargy must have his quiet course:</span><br>
<span name="4.1.65">If not, he foams at mouth and by and by</span><br>
<span name="4.1.66">Breaks out to savage madness. Look he stirs:</span><br>
<span name="4.1.67">Do you withdraw yourself a little while,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.68">He will recover straight: when he is gone,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.69">I would on great occasion speak with you.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit CASSIO</i></p>
<span name="4.1.70">How is it, general? have you not hurt your head?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.71">Dost thou mock me?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.72">                  I mock you! no, by heaven.</span><br>
<span name="4.1.73">Would you would bear your fortune like a man!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.74">A horned man's a monster and a beast.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.75">There's many a beast then in a populous city,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.76">And many a civil monster.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.77">Did he confess it?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.78">                  Good sir, be a man;</span><br>
<span name="4.1.79">Think every bearded fellow that's but yoked</span><br>
<span name="4.1.80">May draw with you: there's millions now alive</span><br>
<span name="4.1.81">That nightly lie in those unproper beds</span><br>
<span name="4.1.82">Which they dare swear peculiar: your case is better.</span><br>
<span name="4.1.83">O, 'tis the spite of hell, the fiend's arch-mock,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.84">To lip a wanton in a secure couch,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.85">And to suppose her chaste! No, let me know;</span><br>
<span name="4.1.86">And knowing what I am, I know what she shall be.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.87">O, thou art wise; 'tis certain.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.88">Stand you awhile apart;</span><br>
<span name="4.1.89">Confine yourself but in a patient list.</span><br>
<span name="4.1.90">Whilst you were here o'erwhelmed with your grief--</span><br>
<span name="4.1.91">A passion most unsuiting such a man--</span><br>
<span name="4.1.92">Cassio came hither: I shifted him away,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.93">And laid good 'scuse upon your ecstasy,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.94">Bade him anon return and here speak with me;</span><br>
<span name="4.1.95">The which he promised. Do but encave yourself,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.96">And mark the fleers, the gibes, and notable scorns,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.97">That dwell in every region of his face;</span><br>
<span name="4.1.98">For I will make him tell the tale anew,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.99">Where, how, how oft, how long ago, and when</span><br>
<span name="4.1.100">He hath, and is again to cope your wife:</span><br>
<span name="4.1.101">I say, but mark his gesture. Marry, patience;</span><br>
<span name="4.1.102">Or I shall say you are all in all in spleen,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.103">And nothing of a man.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.104">Dost thou hear, Iago?</span><br>
<span name="4.1.105">I will be found most cunning in my patience;</span><br>
<span name="4.1.106">But--dost thou hear?--most bloody.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.107">That's not amiss;</span><br>
<span name="4.1.108">But yet keep time in all. Will you withdraw?</span><br>
<p><i>OTHELLO retires</i></p>
<span name="4.1.109">Now will I question Cassio of Bianca,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.110">A housewife that by selling her desires</span><br>
<span name="4.1.111">Buys herself bread and clothes: it is a creature</span><br>
<span name="4.1.112">That dotes on Cassio; as 'tis the strumpet's plague</span><br>
<span name="4.1.113">To beguile many and be beguiled by one:</span><br>
<span name="4.1.114">He, when he hears of her, cannot refrain</span><br>
<span name="4.1.115">From the excess of laughter. Here he comes:</span><br>
<p><i>Re-enter CASSIO</i></p>
<span name="4.1.116">As he shall smile, Othello shall go mad;</span><br>
<span name="4.1.117">And his unbookish jealousy must construe</span><br>
<span name="4.1.118">Poor Cassio's smiles, gestures and light behavior,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.119">Quite in the wrong. How do you now, lieutenant?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.120">The worser that you give me the addition</span><br>
<span name="4.1.121">Whose want even kills me.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.122">Ply Desdemona well, and you are sure on't.</span><br>
<p><i>Speaking lower</i></p>
<span name="4.1.123">Now, if this suit lay in Bianco's power,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.124">How quickly should you speed!</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.125">Alas, poor caitiff!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.126">Look, how he laughs already!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.127">I never knew woman love man so.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.128">Alas, poor rogue! I think, i' faith, she loves me.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.129">Now he denies it faintly, and laughs it out.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.130">Do you hear, Cassio?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.131">Now he importunes him</span><br>
<span name="4.1.132">To tell it o'er: go to; well said, well said.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.133">She gives it out that you shall marry hey:</span><br>
<span name="4.1.134">Do you intend it?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.135">Ha, ha, ha!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.136">Do you triumph, Roman? do you triumph?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.137">I marry her! what? a customer! Prithee, bear some</span><br>
<span name="4.1.138">charity to my wit: do not think it so unwholesome.</span><br>
<span name="4.1.139">Ha, ha, ha!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.140">So, so, so, so: they laugh that win.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.141">'Faith, the cry goes that you shall marry her.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.142">Prithee, say true.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.143">I am a very villain else.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.144">Have you scored me? Well.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.145">This is the monkey's own giving out: she is</span><br>
<span name="4.1.146">persuaded I will marry her, out of her own love and</span><br>
<span name="4.1.147">flattery, not out of my promise.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.148">Iago beckons me; now he begins the story.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.149">She was here even now; she haunts me in every place.</span><br>
<span name="4.1.150">I was the other day talking on the sea-bank with</span><br>
<span name="4.1.151">certain Venetians; and thither comes the bauble,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.152">and, by this hand, she falls me thus about my neck--</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.153">Crying 'O dear Cassio!' as it were: his gesture</span><br>
<span name="4.1.154">imports it.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.155">So hangs, and lolls, and weeps upon me; so hales,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.156">and pulls me: ha, ha, ha!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.157">Now he tells how she plucked him to my chamber. O,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.158">I see that nose of yours, but not that dog I shall</span><br>
<span name="4.1.159">throw it to.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.160">Well, I must leave her company.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.161">Before me! look, where she comes.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.162">'Tis such another fitchew! marry a perfumed one.</span><br>
<p><i>Enter BIANCA</i></p>
<span name="4.1.163">What do you mean by this haunting of me?</span><br>
<br>

<b>BIANCA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.164">Let the devil and his dam haunt you! What did you</span><br>
<span name="4.1.165">mean by that same handkerchief you gave me even now?</span><br>
<span name="4.1.166">I was a fine fool to take it. I must take out the</span><br>
<span name="4.1.167">work?--A likely piece of work, that you should find</span><br>
<span name="4.1.168">it in your chamber, and not know who left it there!</span><br>
<span name="4.1.169">This is some minx's token, and I must take out the</span><br>
<span name="4.1.170">work? There; give it your hobby-horse: wheresoever</span><br>
<span name="4.1.171">you had it, I'll take out no work on't.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.172">How now, my sweet Bianca! how now! how now!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.173">By heaven, that should be my handkerchief!</span><br>
<br>

<b>BIANCA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.174">An you'll come to supper to-night, you may; an you</span><br>
<span name="4.1.175">will not, come when you are next prepared for.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.176">After her, after her.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.177">'Faith, I must; she'll rail in the street else.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.178">Will you sup there?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.179">'Faith, I intend so.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.180">Well, I may chance to see you; for I would very fain</span><br>
<span name="4.1.181">speak with you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.182">Prithee, come; will you?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.183">Go to; say no more.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit CASSIO</i></p>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.184">[Advancing]  How shall I murder him, Iago?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.185">Did you perceive how he laughed at his vice?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.186">O Iago!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.187">And did you see the handkerchief?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.188">Was that mine?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.189">Yours by this hand: and to see how he prizes the</span><br>
<span name="4.1.190">foolish woman your wife! she gave it him, and he</span><br>
<span name="4.1.191">hath given it his whore.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.192">I would have him nine years a-killing.</span><br>
<span name="4.1.193">A fine woman! a fair woman! a sweet woman!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.194">Nay, you must forget that.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.195">Ay, let her rot, and perish, and be damned to-night;</span><br>
<span name="4.1.196">for she shall not live: no, my heart is turned to</span><br>
<span name="4.1.197">stone; I strike it, and it hurts my hand. O, the</span><br>
<span name="4.1.198">world hath not a sweeter creature: she might lie by</span><br>
<span name="4.1.199">an emperor's side and command him tasks.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.200">Nay, that's not your way.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.201">Hang her! I do but say what she is: so delicate</span><br>
<span name="4.1.202">with her needle: an admirable musician: O! she</span><br>
<span name="4.1.203">will sing the savageness out of a bear: of so high</span><br>
<span name="4.1.204">and plenteous wit and invention:--</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.205">She's the worse for all this.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.206">O, a thousand thousand times: and then, of so</span><br>
<span name="4.1.207">gentle a condition!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.208">Ay, too gentle.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.209">Nay, that's certain: but yet the pity of it, Iago!</span><br>
<span name="4.1.210">O Iago, the pity of it, Iago!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.211">If you are so fond over her iniquity, give her</span><br>
<span name="4.1.212">patent to offend; for, if it touch not you, it comes</span><br>
<span name="4.1.213">near nobody.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.214">I will chop her into messes: cuckold me!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.215">O, 'tis foul in her.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.216">With mine officer!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.217">That's fouler.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.218">Get me some poison, Iago; this night: I'll not</span><br>
<span name="4.1.219">expostulate with her, lest her body and beauty</span><br>
<span name="4.1.220">unprovide my mind again: this night, Iago.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.221">Do it not with poison, strangle her in her bed, even</span><br>
<span name="4.1.222">the bed she hath contaminated.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.223">Good, good: the justice of it pleases: very good.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.224">And for Cassio, let me be his undertaker: you</span><br>
<span name="4.1.225">shall hear more by midnight.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.226">Excellent good.</span><br>
<p><i>A trumpet within</i></p>
<span name="4.1.227">What trumpet is that same?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.228">Something from Venice, sure. 'Tis Lodovico</span><br>
<span name="4.1.229">Come from the duke: and, see, your wife is with him.</span><br>
<p><i>Enter LODOVICO, DESDEMONA, and Attendants</i></p>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.230">Save you, worthy general!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.231">With all my heart, sir.</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.232">The duke and senators of Venice greet you.</span><br>
<p><i>Gives him a letter</i></p>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.233">I kiss the instrument of their pleasures.</span><br>
<p><i>Opens the letter, and reads</i></p>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.234">And what's the news, good cousin Lodovico?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.235">I am very glad to see you, signior</span><br>
<span name="4.1.236">Welcome to Cyprus.</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.237">I thank you. How does Lieutenant Cassio?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.238">Lives, sir.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.239">Cousin, there's fall'n between him and my lord</span><br>
<span name="4.1.240">An unkind breach: but you shall make all well.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.241">Are you sure of that?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.242">My lord?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.243">[Reads]  'This fail you not to do, as you will--'</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.244">He did not call; he's busy in the paper.</span><br>
<span name="4.1.245">Is there division 'twixt my lord and Cassio?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.246">A most unhappy one: I would do much</span><br>
<span name="4.1.247">To atone them, for the love I bear to Cassio.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.248">Fire and brimstone!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.249">My lord?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.250">       Are you wise?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.251">What, is he angry?</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.252">                  May be the letter moved him;</span><br>
<span name="4.1.253">For, as I think, they do command him home,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.254">Deputing Cassio in his government.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.255">Trust me, I am glad on't.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.256">Indeed!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.257">My lord?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.258">I am glad to see you mad.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.259">Why, sweet Othello,--</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.260">[Striking her]  Devil!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.261">I have not deserved this.</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.262">My lord, this would not be believed in Venice,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.263">Though I should swear I saw't: 'tis very much:</span><br>
<span name="4.1.264">Make her amends; she weeps.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.265">O devil, devil!</span><br>
<span name="4.1.266">If that the earth could teem with woman's tears,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.267">Each drop she falls would prove a crocodile.</span><br>
<span name="4.1.268">Out of my sight!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.269">I will not stay to offend you.</span><br>
<p><i>Going</i></p>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.270">Truly, an obedient lady:</span><br>
<span name="4.1.271">I do beseech your lordship, call her back.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.272">Mistress!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.273">        My lord?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.274">What would you with her, sir?</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.275">Who, I, my lord?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.276">Ay; you did wish that I would make her turn:</span><br>
<span name="4.1.277">Sir, she can turn, and turn, and yet go on,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.278">And turn again; and she can weep, sir, weep;</span><br>
<span name="4.1.279">And she's obedient, as you say, obedient,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.280">Very obedient. Proceed you in your tears.</span><br>
<span name="4.1.281">Concerning this, sir,--O  well-painted passion!--</span><br>
<span name="4.1.282">I am commanded home. Get you away;</span><br>
<span name="4.1.283">I'll send for you anon. Sir, I obey the mandate,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.284">And will return to Venice. Hence, avaunt!</span><br>
<p><i>Exit DESDEMONA</i></p>
<span name="4.1.285">Cassio shall have my place. And, sir, tonight,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.286">I do entreat that we may sup together:</span><br>
<span name="4.1.287">You are welcome, sir, to Cyprus.--Goats and monkeys!</span><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.288">Is this the noble Moor whom our full senate</span><br>
<span name="4.1.289">Call all in all sufficient? Is this the nature</span><br>
<span name="4.1.290">Whom passion could not shake? whose solid virtue</span><br>
<span name="4.1.291">The shot of accident, nor dart of chance,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.292">Could neither graze nor pierce?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.293">He is much changed.</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.294">Are his wits safe? is he not light of brain?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.295">He's that he is: I may not breathe my censure</span><br>
<span name="4.1.296">What he might be: if what he might he is not,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.297">I would to heaven he were!</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.298">What, strike his wife!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.299">'Faith, that was not so well; yet would I knew</span><br>
<span name="4.1.300">That stroke would prove the worst!</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.301">Is it his use?</span><br>
<span name="4.1.302">Or did the letters work upon his blood,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.303">And new-create this fault?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.304">Alas, alas!</span><br>
<span name="4.1.305">It is not honesty in me to speak</span><br>
<span name="4.1.306">What I have seen and known. You shall observe him,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.307">And his own courses will denote him so</span><br>
<span name="4.1.308">That I may save my speech: do but go after,</span><br>
<span name="4.1.309">And mark how he continues.</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.1.310">I am sorry that I am deceived in him.</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
<br>
<h3>SCENE II. A room in the castle.</h3>
<p></p><br>
<i>Enter OTHELLO and EMILIA</i>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.1">You have seen nothing then?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.2">Nor ever heard, nor ever did suspect.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.3">Yes, you have seen Cassio and she together.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.4">But then I saw no harm, and then I heard</span><br>
<span name="4.2.5">Each syllable that breath made up between them.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.6">What, did they never whisper?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.7">Never, my lord.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.8">Nor send you out o' the way?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.9">Never.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.10">To fetch her fan, her gloves, her mask, nor nothing?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.11">Never, my lord.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.12">That's strange.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.13">I durst, my lord, to wager she is honest,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.14">Lay down my soul at stake: if you think other,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.15">Remove your thought; it doth abuse your bosom.</span><br>
<span name="4.2.16">If any wretch have put this in your head,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.17">Let heaven requite it with the serpent's curse!</span><br>
<span name="4.2.18">For, if she be not honest, chaste, and true,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.19">There's no man happy; the purest of their wives</span><br>
<span name="4.2.20">Is foul as slander.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.21">Bid her come hither: go.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit EMILIA</i></p>
<span name="4.2.22">She says enough; yet she's a simple bawd</span><br>
<span name="4.2.23">That cannot say as much. This is a subtle whore,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.24">A closet lock and key of villanous secrets</span><br>
<span name="4.2.25">And yet she'll kneel and pray; I have seen her do't.</span><br>
<p><i>Enter DESDEMONA with EMILIA</i></p>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.26">My lord, what is your will?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.27">Pray, chuck, come hither.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.28">What is your pleasure?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.29">Let me see your eyes;</span><br>
<span name="4.2.30">Look in my face.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.31">                  What horrible fancy's this?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.32">[To EMILIA]  Some of your function, mistress;</span><br>
<span name="4.2.33">Leave procreants alone and shut the door;</span><br>
<span name="4.2.34">Cough, or cry 'hem,' if any body come:</span><br>
<span name="4.2.35">Your mystery, your mystery: nay, dispatch.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit EMILIA</i></p>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.36">Upon my knees, what doth your speech import?</span><br>
<span name="4.2.37">I understand a fury in your words.</span><br>
<span name="4.2.38">But not the words.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.39">Why, what art thou?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.40">Your wife, my lord; your true</span><br>
<span name="4.2.41">And loyal wife.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.42">                  Come, swear it, damn thyself</span><br>
<span name="4.2.43">Lest, being like one of heaven, the devils themselves</span><br>
<span name="4.2.44">Should fear to seize thee: therefore be double damn'd:</span><br>
<span name="4.2.45">Swear thou art honest.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.46">Heaven doth truly know it.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.47">Heaven truly knows that thou art false as hell.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.48">To whom, my lord? with whom? how am I false?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.49">O Desdemona! away! away! away!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.50">Alas the heavy day! Why do you weep?</span><br>
<span name="4.2.51">Am I the motive of these tears, my lord?</span><br>
<span name="4.2.52">If haply you my father do suspect</span><br>
<span name="4.2.53">An instrument of this your calling back,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.54">Lay not your blame on me: If you have lost him,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.55">Why, I have lost him too.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.56">Had it pleased heaven</span><br>
<span name="4.2.57">To try me with affliction; had they rain'd</span><br>
<span name="4.2.58">All kinds of sores and shames on my bare head.</span><br>
<span name="4.2.59">Steep'd me in poverty to the very lips,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.60">Given to captivity me and my utmost hopes,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.61">I should have found in some place of my soul</span><br>
<span name="4.2.62">A drop of patience: but, alas, to make me</span><br>
<span name="4.2.63">A fixed figure for the time of scorn</span><br>
<span name="4.2.64">To point his slow unmoving finger at!</span><br>
<span name="4.2.65">Yet could I bear that too; well, very well:</span><br>
<span name="4.2.66">But there, where I have garner'd up my heart,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.67">Where either I must live, or bear no life;</span><br>
<span name="4.2.68">The fountain from the which my current runs,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.69">Or else dries up; to be discarded thence!</span><br>
<span name="4.2.70">Or keep it as a cistern for foul toads</span><br>
<span name="4.2.71">To knot and gender in! Turn thy complexion there,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.72">Patience, thou young and rose-lipp'd cherubin,--</span><br>
<span name="4.2.73">Ay, there, look grim as hell!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.74">I hope my noble lord esteems me honest.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.75">O, ay; as summer flies are in the shambles,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.76">That quicken even with blowing. O thou weed,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.77">Who art so lovely fair and smell'st so sweet</span><br>
<span name="4.2.78">That the sense aches at thee, would thou hadst</span><br>
<span name="4.2.79">ne'er been born!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.80">Alas, what ignorant sin have I committed?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.81">Was this fair paper, this most goodly book,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.82">Made to write 'whore' upon? What committed!</span><br>
<span name="4.2.83">Committed! O thou public commoner!</span><br>
<span name="4.2.84">I should make very forges of my cheeks,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.85">That would to cinders burn up modesty,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.86">Did I but speak thy deeds. What committed!</span><br>
<span name="4.2.87">Heaven stops the nose at it and the moon winks,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.88">The bawdy wind that kisses all it meets</span><br>
<span name="4.2.89">Is hush'd within the hollow mine of earth,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.90">And will not hear it. What committed!</span><br>
<span name="4.2.91">Impudent strumpet!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.92">                  By heaven, you do me wrong.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.93">Are you not a strumpet?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.94">No, as I am a Christian:</span><br>
<span name="4.2.95">If to preserve this vessel for my lord</span><br>
<span name="4.2.96">From any other foul unlawful touch</span><br>
<span name="4.2.97">Be not to be a strumpet, I am none.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.98">What, not a whore?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.99">                  No, as I shall be saved.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.100">Is't possible?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.101">                  O, heaven forgive us!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.102">I cry you mercy, then:</span><br>
<span name="4.2.103">I took you for that cunning whore of Venice</span><br>
<span name="4.2.104">That married with Othello.</span><br>
<p><i>Raising his voice</i></p>
<span name="4.2.105">You, mistress,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.106">That have the office opposite to Saint Peter,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.107">And keep the gate of hell!</span><br>
<p><i>Re-enter EMILIA</i></p>
<span name="4.2.108">You, you, ay, you!</span><br>
<span name="4.2.109">We have done our course; there's money for your pains:</span><br>
<span name="4.2.110">I pray you, turn the key and keep our counsel.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.111">Alas, what does this gentleman conceive?</span><br>
<span name="4.2.112">How do you, madam? how do you, my good lady?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.113">'Faith, half asleep.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.114">Good madam, what's the matter with my lord?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.115">With who?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.116">Why, with my lord, madam.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.117">Who is thy lord?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.118">                  He that is yours, sweet lady.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.119">I have none: do not talk to me, Emilia;</span><br>
<span name="4.2.120">I cannot weep; nor answer have I none,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.121">But what should go by water. Prithee, tonight</span><br>
<span name="4.2.122">Lay on my bed my wedding sheets: remember;</span><br>
<span name="4.2.123">And call thy husband hither.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.124">Here's a change indeed!</span><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.125">'Tis meet I should be used so, very meet.</span><br>
<span name="4.2.126">How have I been behaved, that he might stick</span><br>
<span name="4.2.127">The small'st opinion on my least misuse?</span><br>
<p><i>Re-enter EMILIA with IAGO</i></p>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.128">What is your pleasure, madam?</span><br>
<span name="4.2.129">How is't with you?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.130">I cannot tell. Those that do teach young babes</span><br>
<span name="4.2.131">Do it with gentle means and easy tasks:</span><br>
<span name="4.2.132">He might have chid me so; for, in good faith,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.133">I am a child to chiding.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.134">What's the matter, lady?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.135">Alas, Iago, my lord hath so bewhored her.</span><br>
<span name="4.2.136">Thrown such despite and heavy terms upon her,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.137">As true hearts cannot bear.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.138">Am I that name, Iago?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.139">What name, fair lady?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.140">Such as she says my lord did say I was.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.141">He call'd her whore: a beggar in his drink</span><br>
<span name="4.2.142">Could not have laid such terms upon his callat.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.143">Why did he so?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.144">I do not know; I am sure I am none such.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.145">Do not weep, do not weep. Alas the day!</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.146">Hath she forsook so many noble matches,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.147">Her father and her country and her friends,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.148">To be call'd whore? would it not make one weep?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.149">It is my wretched fortune.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.150">Beshrew him for't!</span><br>
<span name="4.2.151">How comes this trick upon him?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.152">Nay, heaven doth know.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.153">I will be hang'd, if some eternal villain,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.154">Some busy and insinuating rogue,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.155">Some cogging, cozening slave, to get some office,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.156">Have not devised this slander; I'll be hang'd else.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.157">Fie, there is no such man; it is impossible.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.158">If any such there be, heaven pardon him!</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.159">A halter pardon him! and hell gnaw his bones!</span><br>
<span name="4.2.160">Why should he call her whore? who keeps her company?</span><br>
<span name="4.2.161">What place? what time? what form? what likelihood?</span><br>
<span name="4.2.162">The Moor's abused by some most villanous knave,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.163">Some base notorious knave, some scurvy fellow.</span><br>
<span name="4.2.164">O heaven, that such companions thou'ldst unfold,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.165">And put in every honest hand a whip</span><br>
<span name="4.2.166">To lash the rascals naked through the world</span><br>
<span name="4.2.167">Even from the east to the west!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.168">Speak within door.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.169">O, fie upon them! Some such squire he was</span><br>
<span name="4.2.170">That turn'd your wit the seamy side without,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.171">And made you to suspect me with the Moor.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.172">You are a fool; go to.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.173">O good Iago,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.174">What shall I do to win my lord again?</span><br>
<span name="4.2.175">Good friend, go to him; for, by this light of heaven,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.176">I know not how I lost him. Here I kneel:</span><br>
<span name="4.2.177">If e'er my will did trespass 'gainst his love,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.178">Either in discourse of thought or actual deed,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.179">Or that mine eyes, mine ears, or any sense,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.180">Delighted them in any other form;</span><br>
<span name="4.2.181">Or that I do not yet, and ever did.</span><br>
<span name="4.2.182">And ever will--though he do shake me off</span><br>
<span name="4.2.183">To beggarly divorcement--love him dearly,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.184">Comfort forswear me! Unkindness may do much;</span><br>
<span name="4.2.185">And his unkindness may defeat my life,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.186">But never taint my love. I cannot say 'whore:'</span><br>
<span name="4.2.187">It does abhor me now I speak the word;</span><br>
<span name="4.2.188">To do the act that might the addition earn</span><br>
<span name="4.2.189">Not the world's mass of vanity could make me.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.190">I pray you, be content; 'tis but his humour:</span><br>
<span name="4.2.191">The business of the state does him offence,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.192">And he does chide with you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.193">If 'twere no other--</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.194">'Tis but so, I warrant.</span><br>
<p><i>Trumpets within</i></p>
<span name="4.2.195">Hark, how these instruments summon to supper!</span><br>
<span name="4.2.196">The messengers of Venice stay the meat;</span><br>
<span name="4.2.197">Go in, and weep not; all things shall be well.</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt DESDEMONA and EMILIA</i></p>
<p><i>Enter RODERIGO</i></p>
<span name="4.2.198">How now, Roderigo!</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.199">I do not find that thou dealest justly with me.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.200">What in the contrary?</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.201">Every day thou daffest me with some device, Iago;</span><br>
<span name="4.2.202">and rather, as it seems to me now, keepest from me</span><br>
<span name="4.2.203">all conveniency than suppliest me with the least</span><br>
<span name="4.2.204">advantage of hope. I will indeed no longer endure</span><br>
<span name="4.2.205">it, nor am I yet persuaded to put up in peace what</span><br>
<span name="4.2.206">already I have foolishly suffered.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.207">Will you hear me, Roderigo?</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.208">'Faith, I have heard too much, for your words and</span><br>
<span name="4.2.209">performances are no kin together.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.210">You charge me most unjustly.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.211">With nought but truth. I have wasted myself out of</span><br>
<span name="4.2.212">my means. The jewels you have had from me to</span><br>
<span name="4.2.213">deliver to Desdemona would half have corrupted a</span><br>
<span name="4.2.214">votarist: you have told me she hath received them</span><br>
<span name="4.2.215">and returned me expectations and comforts of sudden</span><br>
<span name="4.2.216">respect and acquaintance, but I find none.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.217">Well; go to; very well.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.218">Very well! go to! I cannot go to, man; nor 'tis</span><br>
<span name="4.2.219">not very well: nay, I think it is scurvy, and begin</span><br>
<span name="4.2.220">to find myself fobbed in it.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.221">Very well.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.222">I tell you 'tis not very well. I will make myself</span><br>
<span name="4.2.223">known to Desdemona: if she will return me my</span><br>
<span name="4.2.224">jewels, I will give over my suit and repent my</span><br>
<span name="4.2.225">unlawful solicitation; if not, assure yourself I</span><br>
<span name="4.2.226">will seek satisfaction of you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.227">You have said now.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.228">Ay, and said nothing but what I protest intendment of doing.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.229">Why, now I see there's mettle in thee, and even from</span><br>
<span name="4.2.230">this instant to build on thee a better opinion than</span><br>
<span name="4.2.231">ever before. Give me thy hand, Roderigo: thou hast</span><br>
<span name="4.2.232">taken against me a most just exception; but yet, I</span><br>
<span name="4.2.233">protest, I have dealt most directly in thy affair.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.234">It hath not appeared.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.235">I grant indeed it hath not appeared, and your</span><br>
<span name="4.2.236">suspicion is not without wit and judgment. But,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.237">Roderigo, if thou hast that in thee indeed, which I</span><br>
<span name="4.2.238">have greater reason to believe now than ever, I mean</span><br>
<span name="4.2.239">purpose, courage and valour, this night show it: if</span><br>
<span name="4.2.240">thou the next night following enjoy not Desdemona,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.241">take me from this world with treachery and devise</span><br>
<span name="4.2.242">engines for my life.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.243">Well, what is it? is it within reason and compass?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.244">Sir, there is especial commission come from Venice</span><br>
<span name="4.2.245">to depute Cassio in Othello's place.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.246">Is that true? why, then Othello and Desdemona</span><br>
<span name="4.2.247">return again to Venice.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.248">O, no; he goes into Mauritania and takes away with</span><br>
<span name="4.2.249">him the fair Desdemona, unless his abode be</span><br>
<span name="4.2.250">lingered here by some accident: wherein none can be</span><br>
<span name="4.2.251">so determinate as the removing of Cassio.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.252">How do you mean, removing of him?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.253">Why, by making him uncapable of Othello's place;</span><br>
<span name="4.2.254">knocking out his brains.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.255">And that you would have me to do?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.256">Ay, if you dare do yourself a profit and a right.</span><br>
<span name="4.2.257">He sups to-night with a harlotry, and thither will I</span><br>
<span name="4.2.258">go to him: he knows not yet of his horrorable</span><br>
<span name="4.2.259">fortune. If you will watch his going thence, which</span><br>
<span name="4.2.260">I will fashion to fall out between twelve and one,</span><br>
<span name="4.2.261">you may take him at your pleasure: I will be near</span><br>
<span name="4.2.262">to second your attempt, and he shall fall between</span><br>
<span name="4.2.263">us. Come, stand not amazed at it, but go along with</span><br>
<span name="4.2.264">me; I will show you such a necessity in his death</span><br>
<span name="4.2.265">that you shall think yourself bound to put it on</span><br>
<span name="4.2.266">him. It is now high suppertime, and the night grows</span><br>
<span name="4.2.267">to waste: about it.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.268">I will hear further reason for this.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.2.269">And you shall be satisfied.</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
<br>
<h3>SCENE III. Another room In the castle.</h3>
<p></p><br>
<i>Enter OTHELLO, LODOVICO, DESDEMONA, EMILIA and Attendants</i>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.1">I do beseech you, sir, trouble yourself no further.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.2">O, pardon me: 'twill do me good to walk.</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.3">Madam, good night; I humbly thank your ladyship.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.4">Your honour is most welcome.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.5">Will you walk, sir?</span><br>
<span name="4.3.6">O,--Desdemona,--</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.7">My lord?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.8">Get you to bed on the instant; I will be returned</span><br>
<span name="4.3.9">forthwith: dismiss your attendant there: look it be done.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.10">I will, my lord.</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt OTHELLO, LODOVICO, and Attendants</i></p>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.11">How goes it now? he looks gentler than he did.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.12">He says he will return incontinent:</span><br>
<span name="4.3.13">He hath commanded me to go to bed,</span><br>
<span name="4.3.14">And bade me to dismiss you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.15">Dismiss me!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.16">It was his bidding: therefore, good Emilia,.</span><br>
<span name="4.3.17">Give me my nightly wearing, and adieu:</span><br>
<span name="4.3.18">We must not now displease him.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
