<span name="4.3.19">I would you had never seen him!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.20">So would not I	my love doth so approve him,</span><br>
<span name="4.3.21">That even his stubbornness, his cheques, his frowns--</span><br>
<span name="4.3.22">Prithee, unpin me,--have grace and favour in them.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.23">I have laid those sheets you bade me on the bed.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.24">All's one. Good faith, how foolish are our minds!</span><br>
<span name="4.3.25">If I do die before thee prithee, shroud me</span><br>
<span name="4.3.26">In one of those same sheets.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.27">Come, come you talk.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.28">My mother had a maid call'd Barbara:</span><br>
<span name="4.3.29">She was in love, and he she loved proved mad</span><br>
<span name="4.3.30">And did forsake her: she had a song of 'willow;'</span><br>
<span name="4.3.31">An old thing 'twas, but it express'd her fortune,</span><br>
<span name="4.3.32">And she died singing it: that song to-night</span><br>
<span name="4.3.33">Will not go from my mind; I have much to do,</span><br>
<span name="4.3.34">But to go hang my head all at one side,</span><br>
<span name="4.3.35">And sing it like poor Barbara. Prithee, dispatch.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.36">Shall I go fetch your night-gown?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.37">No, unpin me here.</span><br>
<span name="4.3.38">This Lodovico is a proper man.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.39">A very handsome man.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.40">He speaks well.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.41">I know a lady in Venice would have walked barefoot</span><br>
<span name="4.3.42">to Palestine for a touch of his nether lip.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.43">[Singing]  The poor soul sat sighing by a sycamore tree,</span><br>
<span name="4.3.44">Sing all a green willow:</span><br>
<span name="4.3.45">Her hand on her bosom, her head on her knee,</span><br>
<span name="4.3.46">Sing willow, willow, willow:</span><br>
<span name="4.3.47">The fresh streams ran by her, and murmur'd her moans;</span><br>
<span name="4.3.48">Sing willow, willow, willow;</span><br>
<span name="4.3.49">Her salt tears fell from her, and soften'd the stones;</span><br>
<span name="4.3.50">Lay by these:--</span><br>
<p><i>Singing</i></p>
<span name="4.3.51">Sing willow, willow, willow;</span><br>
<span name="4.3.52">Prithee, hie thee; he'll come anon:--</span><br>
<p><i>Singing</i></p>
<span name="4.3.53">Sing all a green willow must be my garland.</span><br>
<span name="4.3.54">Let nobody blame him; his scorn I approve,-</span><br>
<span name="4.3.55">Nay, that's not next.--Hark! who is't that knocks?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.56">It's the wind.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.57">[Singing]  I call'd my love false love; but what</span><br>
<span name="4.3.58">said he then?</span><br>
<span name="4.3.59">Sing willow, willow, willow:</span><br>
<span name="4.3.60">If I court moe women, you'll couch with moe men!</span><br>
<span name="4.3.61">So, get thee gone; good night Ate eyes do itch;</span><br>
<span name="4.3.62">Doth that bode weeping?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.63">'Tis neither here nor there.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.64">I have heard it said so. O, these men, these men!</span><br>
<span name="4.3.65">Dost thou in conscience think,--tell me, Emilia,--</span><br>
<span name="4.3.66">That there be women do abuse their husbands</span><br>
<span name="4.3.67">In such gross kind?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.68">There be some such, no question.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.69">Wouldst thou do such a deed for all the world?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.70">Why, would not you?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.71">No, by this heavenly light!</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.72">Nor I neither by this heavenly light;</span><br>
<span name="4.3.73">I might do't as well i' the dark.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.74">Wouldst thou do such a deed for all the world?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.75">The world's a huge thing: it is a great price.</span><br>
<span name="4.3.76">For a small vice.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.77">In troth, I think thou wouldst not.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.78">In troth, I think I should; and undo't when I had</span><br>
<span name="4.3.79">done. Marry, I would not do such a thing for a</span><br>
<span name="4.3.80">joint-ring, nor for measures of lawn, nor for</span><br>
<span name="4.3.81">gowns, petticoats, nor caps, nor any petty</span><br>
<span name="4.3.82">exhibition; but for the whole world,--why, who would</span><br>
<span name="4.3.83">not make her husband a cuckold to make him a</span><br>
<span name="4.3.84">monarch? I should venture purgatory for't.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.85">Beshrew me, if I would do such a wrong</span><br>
<span name="4.3.86">For the whole world.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.87">Why the wrong is but a wrong i' the world: and</span><br>
<span name="4.3.88">having the world for your labour, tis a wrong in your</span><br>
<span name="4.3.89">own world, and you might quickly make it right.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.90">I do not think there is any such woman.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.91">Yes, a dozen; and as many to the vantage as would</span><br>
<span name="4.3.92">store the world they played for.</span><br>
<span name="4.3.93">But I do think it is their husbands' faults</span><br>
<span name="4.3.94">If wives do fall: say that they slack their duties,</span><br>
<span name="4.3.95">And pour our treasures into foreign laps,</span><br>
<span name="4.3.96">Or else break out in peevish jealousies,</span><br>
<span name="4.3.97">Throwing restraint upon us; or say they strike us,</span><br>
<span name="4.3.98">Or scant our former having in despite;</span><br>
<span name="4.3.99">Why, we have galls, and though we have some grace,</span><br>
<span name="4.3.100">Yet have we some revenge. Let husbands know</span><br>
<span name="4.3.101">Their wives have sense like them: they see and smell</span><br>
<span name="4.3.102">And have their palates both for sweet and sour,</span><br>
<span name="4.3.103">As husbands have. What is it that they do</span><br>
<span name="4.3.104">When they change us for others? Is it sport?</span><br>
<span name="4.3.105">I think it is: and doth affection breed it?</span><br>
<span name="4.3.106">I think it doth: is't frailty that thus errs?</span><br>
<span name="4.3.107">It is so too: and have not we affections,</span><br>
<span name="4.3.108">Desires for sport, and frailty, as men have?</span><br>
<span name="4.3.109">Then let them use us well: else let them know,</span><br>
<span name="4.3.110">The ills we do, their ills instruct us so.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="4.3.111">Good night, good night: heaven me such uses send,</span><br>
<span name="4.3.112">Not to pick bad from bad, but by bad mend!</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
<br><p>
</p><h3>ACT V</h3>
<h3>SCENE I. Cyprus. A street.</h3>
<p></p><br>
<i>Enter IAGO and RODERIGO</i>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.1">Here, stand behind this bulk; straight will he come:</span><br>
<span name="5.1.2">Wear thy good rapier bare, and put it home:</span><br>
<span name="5.1.3">Quick, quick; fear nothing; I'll be at thy elbow:</span><br>
<span name="5.1.4">It makes us, or it mars us; think on that,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.5">And fix most firm thy resolution.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.6">Be near at hand; I may miscarry in't.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.7">Here, at thy hand: be bold, and take thy stand.</span><br>
<p><i>Retires</i></p>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.8">I have no great devotion to the deed;</span><br>
<span name="5.1.9">And yet he hath given me satisfying reasons:</span><br>
<span name="5.1.10">'Tis but a man gone. Forth, my sword: he dies.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.11">I have rubb'd this young quat almost to the sense,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.12">And he grows angry. Now, whether he kill Cassio,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.13">Or Cassio him, or each do kill the other,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.14">Every way makes my gain: live Roderigo,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.15">He calls me to a restitution large</span><br>
<span name="5.1.16">Of gold and jewels that I bobb'd from him,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.17">As gifts to Desdemona;</span><br>
<span name="5.1.18">It must not be: if Cassio do remain,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.19">He hath a daily beauty in his life</span><br>
<span name="5.1.20">That makes me ugly; and, besides, the Moor</span><br>
<span name="5.1.21">May unfold me to him; there stand I in much peril:</span><br>
<span name="5.1.22">No, he must die. But so: I hear him coming.</span><br>
<p><i>Enter CASSIO</i></p>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.23">I know his gait, 'tis he.--Villain, thou diest!</span><br>
<p><i>Makes a pass at CASSIO</i></p>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.24">That thrust had been mine enemy indeed,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.25">But that my coat is better than thou know'st</span><br>
<span name="5.1.26">I will make proof of thine.</span><br>
<p><i>Draws, and wounds RODERIGO</i></p>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.27">O, I am slain!</span><br>
<p><i>IAGO from behind wounds CASSIO in the leg, and exit</i></p>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.28">I am maim'd for ever. Help, ho! murder! murder!</span><br>
<p><i>Falls</i></p>
<p><i>Enter OTHELLO</i></p>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.29">The voice of Cassio: Iago keeps his word.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.30">O, villain that I am!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.31">It is even so.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.32">O, help, ho! light! a surgeon!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.33">'Tis he:--O brave Iago, honest and just,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.34">That hast such noble sense of thy friend's wrong!</span><br>
<span name="5.1.35">Thou teachest me. Minion, your dear lies dead,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.36">And your unblest fate hies: strumpet, I come.</span><br>
<span name="5.1.37">Forth of my heart those charms, thine eyes, are blotted;</span><br>
<span name="5.1.38">Thy bed, lust-stain'd, shall with lust's blood be spotted.</span><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<p><i>Enter LODOVICO and GRATIANO</i></p>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.39">What, ho! no watch? no passage? murder! murder!</span><br>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.40">'Tis some mischance; the cry is very direful.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.41">O, help!</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.42">Hark!</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.43">O wretched villain!</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.44">Two or three groan: it is a heavy night:</span><br>
<span name="5.1.45">These may be counterfeits: let's think't unsafe</span><br>
<span name="5.1.46">To come in to the cry without more help.</span><br>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.47">Nobody come? then shall I bleed to death.</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.48">Hark!</span><br>
<p><i>Re-enter IAGO, with a light</i></p>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.49">Here's one comes in his shirt, with light and weapons.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.50">Who's there? whose noise is this that ones on murder?</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.51">We do not know.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.52">                  Did not you hear a cry?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.53">Here, here! for heaven's sake, help me!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.54">What's the matter?</span><br>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.55">This is Othello's ancient, as I take it.</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.56">The same indeed; a very valiant fellow.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.57">What are you here that cry so grievously?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.58">Iago? O, I am spoil'd, undone by villains!</span><br>
<span name="5.1.59">Give me some help.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.60">O me, lieutenant! what villains have done this?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.61">I think that one of them is hereabout,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.62">And cannot make away.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.63">O treacherous villains!</span><br>
<span name="5.1.64">What are you there? come in, and give some help.</span><br>
<p><i>To LODOVICO and GRATIANO</i></p>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.65">O, help me here!</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.66">That's one of them.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.67">O murderous slave! O villain!</span><br>
<p><i>Stabs RODERIGO</i></p>
<br>

<b>RODERIGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.68">O damn'd Iago! O inhuman dog!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.69">Kill men i' the dark!--Where be these bloody thieves?--</span><br>
<span name="5.1.70">How silent is this town!--Ho! murder! murder!--</span><br>
<span name="5.1.71">What may you be? are you of good or evil?</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.72">As you shall prove us, praise us.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.73">Signior Lodovico?</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.74">He, sir.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.75">I cry you mercy. Here's Cassio hurt by villains.</span><br>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.76">Cassio!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.77">How is't, brother!</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.78">My leg is cut in two.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.79">Marry, heaven forbid!</span><br>
<span name="5.1.80">Light, gentlemen; I'll bind it with my shirt.</span><br>
<p><i>Enter BIANCA</i></p>
<br>

<b>BIANCA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.81">What is the matter, ho? who is't that cried?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.82">Who is't that cried!</span><br>
<br>

<b>BIANCA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.83">O my dear Cassio! my sweet Cassio! O Cassio,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.84">Cassio, Cassio!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.85">O notable strumpet! Cassio, may you suspect</span><br>
<span name="5.1.86">Who they should be that have thus many led you?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.87">No.</span><br>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.88">I am to find you thus: I have been to seek you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.89">Lend me a garter. So. O, for a chair,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.90">To bear him easily hence!</span><br>
<br>

<b>BIANCA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.91">Alas, he faints! O Cassio, Cassio, Cassio!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.92">Gentlemen all, I do suspect this trash</span><br>
<span name="5.1.93">To be a party in this injury.</span><br>
<span name="5.1.94">Patience awhile, good Cassio. Come, come;</span><br>
<span name="5.1.95">Lend me a light. Know we this face or no?</span><br>
<span name="5.1.96">Alas my friend and my dear countryman</span><br>
<span name="5.1.97">Roderigo! no:--yes, sure: O heaven! Roderigo.</span><br>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.98">What, of Venice?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.99">Even he, sir; did you know him?</span><br>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.100">Know him! ay.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.101">Signior Gratiano? I cry you gentle pardon;</span><br>
<span name="5.1.102">These bloody accidents must excuse my manners,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.103">That so neglected you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.104">I am glad to see you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.105">How do you, Cassio? O, a chair, a chair!</span><br>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.106">Roderigo!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.107">He, he 'tis he.</span><br>
<p><i>A chair brought in</i></p>
<span name="5.1.108">O, that's well said; the chair!</span><br>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.109">Some good man bear him carefully from hence;</span><br>
<span name="5.1.110">I'll fetch the general's surgeon.</span><br>
<p><i>To BIANCA</i></p>
<span name="5.1.111">For you, mistress,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.112">Save you your labour. He that lies slain</span><br>
<span name="5.1.113">here, Cassio,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.114">Was my dear friend: what malice was between you?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.115">None in the world; nor do I know the man.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.116">[To BIANCA]  What, look you pale? O, bear him out</span><br>
<span name="5.1.117">o' the air.</span><br>
<p><i>CASSIO and RODERIGO are borne off</i></p>
<span name="5.1.118">Stay you, good gentlemen. Look you pale, mistress?</span><br>
<span name="5.1.119">Do you perceive the gastness of her eye?</span><br>
<span name="5.1.120">Nay, if you stare, we shall hear more anon.</span><br>
<span name="5.1.121">Behold her well; I pray you, look upon her:</span><br>
<span name="5.1.122">Do you see, gentlemen? nay, guiltiness will speak,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.123">Though tongues were out of use.</span><br>
<p><i>Enter EMILIA</i></p>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.124">'Las, what's the matter? what's the matter, husband?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.125">Cassio hath here been set on in the dark</span><br>
<span name="5.1.126">By Roderigo and fellows that are scaped:</span><br>
<span name="5.1.127">He's almost slain, and Roderigo dead.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.128">Alas, good gentleman! alas, good Cassio!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.129">This is the fruit of whoring. Prithee, Emilia,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.130">Go know of Cassio where he supp'd to-night.</span><br>
<p><i>To BIANCA</i></p>
<span name="5.1.131">What, do you shake at that?</span><br>
<br>

<b>BIANCA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.132">He supp'd at my house; but I therefore shake not.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.133">O, did he so? I charge you, go with me.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.134">Fie, fie upon thee, strumpet!</span><br>
<br>

<b>BIANCA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.135">I am no strumpet; but of life as honest</span><br>
<span name="5.1.136">As you that thus abuse me.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.137">As I! foh! fie upon thee!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.1.138">Kind gentlemen, let's go see poor Cassio dress'd.</span><br>
<span name="5.1.139">Come, mistress, you must tell's another tale.</span><br>
<span name="5.1.140">Emilia run you to the citadel,</span><br>
<span name="5.1.141">And tell my lord and lady what hath happ'd.</span><br>
<span name="5.1.142">Will you go on? I pray.</span><br>
<p><i>Aside</i></p>
<span name="5.1.143">This is the night</span><br>
<span name="5.1.144">That either makes me or fordoes me quite.</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
<br>
<h3>SCENE II. A bedchamber in the castle: DESDEMONA in bed asleep;</h3>
<br>
<span name="5.2.1">a light burning.</span><br>
<p><i>Enter OTHELLO</i></p>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.2">It is the cause, it is the cause, my soul,--</span><br>
<span name="5.2.3">Let me not name it to you, you chaste stars!--</span><br>
<span name="5.2.4">It is the cause. Yet I'll not shed her blood;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.5">Nor scar that whiter skin of hers than snow,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.6">And smooth as monumental alabaster.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.7">Yet she must die, else she'll betray more men.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.8">Put out the light, and then put out the light:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.9">If I quench thee, thou flaming minister,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.10">I can again thy former light restore,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.11">Should I repent me: but once put out thy light,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.12">Thou cunning'st pattern of excelling nature,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.13">I know not where is that Promethean heat</span><br>
<span name="5.2.14">That can thy light relume. When I have pluck'd the rose,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.15">I cannot give it vital growth again.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.16">It must needs wither: I'll smell it on the tree.</span><br>
<p><i>Kissing her</i></p>
<span name="5.2.17">Ah balmy breath, that dost almost persuade</span><br>
<span name="5.2.18">Justice to break her sword! One more, one more.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.19">Be thus when thou art dead, and I will kill thee,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.20">And love thee after. One more, and this the last:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.21">So sweet was ne'er so fatal. I must weep,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.22">But they are cruel tears: this sorrow's heavenly;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.23">It strikes where it doth love. She wakes.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.24">Who's there? Othello?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.25">Ay. Desdemona.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.26">Will you come to bed, my lord?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.27">Have you pray'd to-night, Desdemona?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.28">Ay, my lord.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.29">If you bethink yourself of any crime</span><br>
<span name="5.2.30">Unreconciled as yet to heaven and grace,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.31">Solicit for it straight.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.32">Alas, my lord, what do you mean by that?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.33">Well, do it, and be brief; I will walk by:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.34">I would not kill thy unprepared spirit;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.35">No; heaven forfend! I would not kill thy soul.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.36">Talk you of killing?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.37">Ay, I do.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.38">Then heaven</span><br>
<span name="5.2.39">Have mercy on me!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.40">                  Amen, with all my heart!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.41">If you say so, I hope you will not kill me.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.42">Hum!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.43">And yet I fear you; for you are fatal then</span><br>
<span name="5.2.44">When your eyes roll so: why I should fear I know not,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.45">Since guiltiness I know not; but yet I feel I fear.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.46">Think on thy sins.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.47">                  They are loves I bear to you.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.48">Ay, and for that thou diest.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.49">That death's unnatural that kills for loving.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.50">Alas, why gnaw you so your nether lip?</span><br>
<span name="5.2.51">Some bloody passion shakes your very frame:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.52">These are portents; but yet I hope, I hope,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.53">They do not point on me.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.54">Peace, and be still!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.55">I will so. What's the matter?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.56">That handkerchief which I so loved and gave thee</span><br>
<span name="5.2.57">Thou gavest to Cassio.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.58">No, by my life and soul!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.59">Send for the man, and ask him.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.60">Sweet soul, take heed,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.61">Take heed of perjury; thou art on thy deathbed.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.62">Ay, but not yet to die.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.63">Yes, presently:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.64">Therefore confess thee freely of thy sin;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.65">For to deny each article with oath</span><br>
<span name="5.2.66">Cannot remove nor choke the strong conception</span><br>
<span name="5.2.67">That I do groan withal. Thou art to die.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.68">Then Lord have mercy on me!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.69">I say, amen.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.70">And have you mercy too! I never did</span><br>
<span name="5.2.71">Offend you in my life; never loved Cassio</span><br>
<span name="5.2.72">But with such general warranty of heaven</span><br>
<span name="5.2.73">As I might love: I never gave him token.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.74">By heaven, I saw my handkerchief in's hand.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.75">O perjured woman! thou dost stone my heart,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.76">And makest me call what I intend to do</span><br>
<span name="5.2.77">A murder, which I thought a sacrifice:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.78">I saw the handkerchief.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.79">He found it then;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.80">I never gave it him: send for him hither;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.81">Let him confess a truth.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.82">He hath confess'd.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.83">What, my lord?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.84">That he hath used thee.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.85">How? unlawfully?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.86">Ay.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.87">He will not say so.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.88">No, his mouth is stopp'd;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.89">Honest Iago hath ta'en order for't.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.90">O! my fear interprets: what, is he dead?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.91">Had all his hairs been lives, my great revenge</span><br>
<span name="5.2.92">Had stomach for them all.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.93">Alas! he is betray'd and I undone.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.94">Out, strumpet! weep'st thou for him to my face?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.95">O, banish me, my lord, but kill me not!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.96">Down, strumpet!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.97">Kill me to-morrow: let me live to-night!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.98">Nay, if you strive--</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.99">But half an hour!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.100">                  Being done, there is no pause.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.101">But while I say one prayer!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.102">It is too late.</span><br>
<p><i>He stifles her</i></p>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.103">[Within]  My lord , my lord! what, ho! my lord, my lord!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.104">What noise is this? Not dead? not yet quite dead?</span><br>
<span name="5.2.105">I that am cruel am yet merciful;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.106">I would not have thee linger in thy pain: So, so.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.107">[Within]  What, ho! my lord, my lord!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.108">Who's there?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.109">[Within]  O, good my lord, I would speak a word with you!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.110">Yes: 'tis Emilia. By and by. She's dead.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.111">'Tis like she comes to speak of Cassio's death.--</span><br>
<span name="5.2.112">The noise was here. Ha! no more moving?</span><br>
<span name="5.2.113">Still as the grave. Shall she come in? were't good?--</span><br>
<span name="5.2.114">I think she stirs again:--no. What's best to do?</span><br>
<span name="5.2.115">If she come in, she'll sure speak to my wife:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.116">My wife! my wife! what wife? I have no wife.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.117">O insupportable! O heavy hour!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.118">Methinks it should be now a huge eclipse</span><br>
<span name="5.2.119">Of sun and moon, and that the affrighted globe</span><br>
<span name="5.2.120">Should yawn at alteration.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.121">[Within]  I do beseech you</span><br>
<span name="5.2.122">That I may speak with you, O, good my lord!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.123">I had forgot thee: O, come in, Emilia;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.124">Soft; by and by. Let me the curtains draw.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.125">Where art thou?</span><br>
<p><i>Unlocks the door</i></p>
<p><i>Enter EMILIA</i></p>
<span name="5.2.126">What's the matter with thee now?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.127">O, my good lord, yonder's foul murders done!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.128">What, now?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.129">But now, my lord.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.130">It is the very error of the moon;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.131">She comes more nearer earth than she was wont,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.132">And makes men mad.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.133">Cassio, my lord, hath kill'd a young Venetian</span><br>
<span name="5.2.134">Call'd Roderigo.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.135">                  Roderigo kill'd!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.136">And Cassio kill'd!</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.137">No, Cassio is not kill'd.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.138">Not Cassio kill'd! then murder's out of tune,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.139">And sweet revenge grows harsh.</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.140">O, falsely, falsely murder'd!</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.141">Alas, what cry is that?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.142">That! what?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.143">Out, and alas! that was my lady's voice.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.144">Help! help, ho! help! O lady, speak again!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.145">Sweet Desdemona! O sweet mistress, speak!</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.146">A guiltless death I die.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.147">O, who hath done this deed?</span><br>
<br>

<b>DESDEMONA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.148">Nobody; I myself. Farewell</span><br>
<span name="5.2.149">Commend me to my kind lord: O, farewell!</span><br>
<p><i>Dies</i></p>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.150">Why, how should she be murder'd?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.151">Alas, who knows?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.152">You heard her say herself, it was not I.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.153">She said so: I must needs report the truth.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.154">She's, like a liar, gone to burning hell:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.155">'Twas I that kill'd her.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.156">O, the more angel she,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.157">And you the blacker devil!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.158">She turn'd to folly, and she was a whore.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.159">Thou dost belie her, and thou art a devil.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.160">She was false as water.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.161">Thou art rash as fire, to say</span><br>
<span name="5.2.162">That she was false: O, she was heavenly true!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.163">Cassio did top her; ask thy husband else.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.164">O, I were damn'd beneath all depth in hell,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.165">But that I did proceed upon just grounds</span><br>
<span name="5.2.166">To this extremity. Thy husband knew it all.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.167">My husband!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.168">Thy husband.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.169">That she was false to wedlock?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.170">Ay, with Cassio. Nay, had she been true,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.171">If heaven would make me such another world</span><br>
<span name="5.2.172">Of one entire and Perfect chrysolite,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.173">I'ld not have sold her for it.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.174">My husband!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.175">          Ay, 'twas he that told me first:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.176">An honest man he is, and hates the slime</span><br>
<span name="5.2.177">That sticks on filthy deeds.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.178">My husband!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.179">What needs this iteration, woman? I say thy husband.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.180">O mistress, villany hath made mocks with love,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.181">My husband say that she was false!</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.182">He, woman;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.183">I say thy husband: dost understand the word?</span><br>
<span name="5.2.184">My friend, thy husband, honest, honest Iago.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.185">If he say so, may his pernicious soul</span><br>
<span name="5.2.186">Rot half a grain a day! he lies to the heart:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.187">She was too fond of her most filthy bargain.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.188">Ha!</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.189">Do thy worst:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.190">This deed of thine is no more worthy heaven</span><br>
<span name="5.2.191">Than thou wast worthy her.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.192">Peace, you were best.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.193">Thou hast not half that power to do me harm</span><br>
<span name="5.2.194">As I have to be hurt. O gull! O dolt!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.195">As ignorant as dirt! thou hast done a deed--</span><br>
<span name="5.2.196">I care not for thy sword; I'll make thee known,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.197">Though I lost twenty lives.--Help! help, ho! help!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.198">The Moor hath kill'd my mistress! Murder! murder!</span><br>
<p><i>Enter MONTANO, GRATIANO, IAGO, and others</i></p>
<br>

<b>MONTANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.199">What is the matter? How now, general!</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.200">O, are you come, Iago? you have done well,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.201">That men must lay their murders on your neck.</span><br>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.202">What is the matter?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.203">Disprove this villain, if thou be'st a man:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.204">He says thou told'st him that his wife was false:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.205">I know thou didst not, thou'rt not such a villain:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.206">Speak, for my heart is full.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.207">I told him what I thought, and told no more</span><br>
<span name="5.2.208">Than what he found himself was apt and true.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.209">But did you ever tell him she was false?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.210">I did.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.211">You told a lie, an odious, damned lie;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.212">Upon my soul, a lie, a wicked lie.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.213">She false with Cassio!--did you say with Cassio?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.214">With Cassio, mistress. Go to, charm your tongue.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.215">I will not charm my tongue; I am bound to speak:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.216">My mistress here lies murder'd in her bed,--</span><br>
<br>

<b>All</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.217">O heavens forfend!</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.218">And your reports have set the murder on.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.219">Nay, stare not, masters: it is true, indeed.</span><br>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.220">'Tis a strange truth.</span><br>
<br>

<b>MONTANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.221">O monstrous act!</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.222">                  Villany, villany, villany!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.223">I think upon't, I think: I smell't: O villany!--</span><br>
<span name="5.2.224">I thought so then:--I'll kill myself for grief:--</span><br>
<span name="5.2.225">O villany, villany!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.226">What, are you mad? I charge you, get you home.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.227">Good gentlemen, let me have leave to speak:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.228">'Tis proper I obey him, but not now.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.229">Perchance, Iago, I will ne'er go home.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.230">O! O! O!</span><br>
<p><i>He falls on the bed</i></p>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.231">       Nay, lay thee down and roar;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.232">For thou hast kill'd the sweetest innocent</span><br>
<span name="5.2.233">That e'er did lift up eye.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.234">[Rising]  O, she was foul!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.235">I scarce did know you, uncle: there lies your niece,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.236">Whose breath, indeed, these hands have newly stopp'd:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.237">I know this act shows horrible and grim.</span><br>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.238">Poor Desdemona! I am glad thy father's dead:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.239">Thy match was mortal to him, and pure grief</span><br>
<span name="5.2.240">Shore his old thread in twain: did he live now,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.241">This sight would make him do a desperate turn,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.242">Yea, curse his better angel from his side,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.243">And fall to reprobation.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.244">'Tis pitiful; but yet Iago knows</span><br>
<span name="5.2.245">That she with Cassio hath the act of shame</span><br>
<span name="5.2.246">A thousand times committed; Cassio confess'd it:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.247">And she did gratify his amorous works</span><br>
<span name="5.2.248">With that recognizance and pledge of love</span><br>
<span name="5.2.249">Which I first gave her; I saw it in his hand:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.250">It was a handkerchief, an antique token</span><br>
<span name="5.2.251">My father gave my mother.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.252">O heaven! O heavenly powers!</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.253">Come, hold your peace.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.254">'Twill out, 'twill out: I peace!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.255">No, I will speak as liberal as the north:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.256">Let heaven and men and devils, let them all,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.257">All, all, cry shame against me, yet I'll speak.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.258">Be wise, and get you home.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.259">I will not.</span><br>
<p><i>IAGO offers to stab EMILIA</i></p>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.260">Fie!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.261">Your sword upon a woman?</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.262">O thou dull Moor! that handkerchief thou speak'st of</span><br>
<span name="5.2.263">I found by fortune and did give my husband;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.264">For often, with a solemn earnestness,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.265">More than indeed belong'd to such a trifle,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.266">He begg'd of me to steal it.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.267">Villanous whore!</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.268">She give it Cassio! no, alas! I found it,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.269">And I did give't my husband.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.270">Filth, thou liest!</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.271">By heaven, I do not, I do not, gentlemen.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.272">O murderous coxcomb! what should such a fool</span><br>
<span name="5.2.273">Do with so good a woman?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.274">Are there no stones in heaven</span><br>
<span name="5.2.275">But what serve for the thunder?--Precious villain!</span><br>
<p><i>He runs at IAGO  IAGO, from behind, stabs EMILIA, and exit</i></p>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.276">The woman falls; sure, he hath kill'd his wife.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.277">Ay, ay: O, lay me by my mistress' side.</span><br>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.278">He's gone, but his wife's kill'd.</span><br>
<br>

<b>MONTANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.279">'Tis a notorious villain. Take you this weapon,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.280">Which I have here recover'd from the Moor:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.281">Come, guard the door without; let him not pass,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.282">But kill him rather. I'll after that same villain,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.283">For 'tis a damned slave.</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt MONTANO and GRATIANO</i></p>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.284">I am not valiant neither,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.285">But ever puny whipster gets my sword:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.286">But why should honour outlive honesty?</span><br>
<span name="5.2.287">Let it go all.</span><br>
<br>

<b>EMILIA</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.288">What did thy song bode, lady?</span><br>
<span name="5.2.289">Hark, canst thou hear me? I will play the swan.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.290">And die in music.</span><br>
<p><i>Singing</i></p>
<span name="5.2.291">Willow, willow, willow,--</span><br>
<span name="5.2.292">Moor, she was chaste; she loved thee, cruel Moor;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.293">So come my soul to bliss, as I speak true;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.294">So speaking as I think, I die, I die.</span><br>
<p><i>Dies</i></p>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.295">I have another weapon in this chamber;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.296">It is a sword of Spain, the ice-brook's temper:--</span><br>
<span name="5.2.297">O, here it is. Uncle, I must come forth.</span><br>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.298">[Within]  If thou attempt it, it will cost thee dear:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.299">Thou hast no weapon, and perforce must suffer.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.300">Look in upon me then and speak with me,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.301">Or, naked as I am, I will assault thee.</span><br>
<p><i>Re-enter GRATIANO</i></p>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.302">What is the matter?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.303">Behold, I have a weapon;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.304">A better never did itself sustain</span><br>
<span name="5.2.305">Upon a soldier's thigh: I have seen the day,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.306">That, with this little arm and this good sword,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.307">I have made my way through more impediments</span><br>
<span name="5.2.308">Than twenty times your stop: but, O vain boast!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.309">Who can control his fate? 'tis not so now.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.310">Be not afraid, though you do see me weapon'd;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.311">Here is my journey's end, here is my butt,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.312">And very sea-mark of my utmost sail.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.313">Do you go back dismay'd? 'tis a lost fear;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.314">Man but a rush against Othello's breast,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.315">And he retires. Where should Othello go?</span><br>
<span name="5.2.316">Now, how dost thou look now? O ill-starr'd wench!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.317">Pale as thy smock! when we shall meet at compt,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.318">This look of thine will hurl my soul from heaven,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.319">And fiends will snatch at it. Cold, cold, my girl!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.320">Even like thy chastity. O cursed slave!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.321">Whip me, ye devils,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.322">From the possession of this heavenly sight!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.323">Blow me about in winds! roast me in sulphur!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.324">Wash me in steep-down gulfs of liquid fire!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.325">O Desdemona! Desdemona! dead!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.326">Oh! Oh! Oh!</span><br>
<p><i>Enter LODOVICO. MONTANO, CASSIO carried in a chair, and Officers with IAGO, prisoner</i></p>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.327">Where is this rash and most unfortunate man?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.328">That's he that was Othello: here I am.</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.329">Where is that viper? bring the villain forth.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.330">I look down towards his feet; but that's a fable.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.331">If that thou best a devil, I cannot kill thee.</span><br>
<p><i>Wounds IAGO</i></p>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.332">Wrench his sword from him.</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.333">I bleed, sir; but not kill'd.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.334">I am not sorry neither: I'ld have thee live;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.335">For, in my sense, 'tis happiness to die.</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.336">O thou Othello, thou wert once so good,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.337">Fall'n in the practise of a damned slave,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.338">What shall be said to thee?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.339">Why, any thing:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.340">An honourable murderer, if you will;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.341">For nought I did in hate, but all in honour.</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.342">This wretch hath part confess'd his villany:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.343">Did you and he consent in Cassio's death?</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.344">Ay.</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.345">Dear general, I never gave you cause.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.346">I do believe it, and I ask your pardon.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.347">Will you, I pray, demand that demi-devil</span><br>
<span name="5.2.348">Why he hath thus ensnared my soul and body?</span><br>
<br>

<b>IAGO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.349">Demand me nothing: what you know, you know:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.350">From this time forth I never will speak word.</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.351">What, not to pray?</span><br>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.352">                  Torments will ope your lips.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.353">Well, thou dost best.</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.354">Sir, you shall understand what hath befall'n,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.355">Which, as I think, you know not. Here is a letter</span><br>
<span name="5.2.356">Found in the pocket of the slain Roderigo;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.357">And here another: the one of them imports</span><br>
<span name="5.2.358">The death of Cassio to be undertook</span><br>
<span name="5.2.359">By Roderigo.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.360">O villain!</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.361">Most heathenish and most gross!</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.362">Now here's another discontented paper,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.363">Found in his pocket too; and this, it seems,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.364">Roderigo meant to have sent this damned villain;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.365">But that belike Iago in the interim</span><br>
<span name="5.2.366">Came in and satisfied him.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.367">O the pernicious caitiff!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.368">How came you, Cassio, by that handkerchief</span><br>
<span name="5.2.369">That was my wife's?</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.370">I found it in my chamber:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.371">And he himself confess'd but even now</span><br>
<span name="5.2.372">That there he dropp'd it for a special purpose</span><br>
<span name="5.2.373">Which wrought to his desire.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.374">O fool! fool! fool!</span><br>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.375">There is besides in Roderigo's letter,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.376">How he upbraids Iago, that he made him</span><br>
<span name="5.2.377">Brave me upon the watch; whereon it came</span><br>
<span name="5.2.378">That I was cast: and even but now he spake,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.379">After long seeming dead, Iago hurt him,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.380">Iago set him on.</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.381">You must forsake this room, and go with us:</span><br>
<span name="5.2.382">Your power and your command is taken off,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.383">And Cassio rules in Cyprus. For this slave,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.384">If there be any cunning cruelty</span><br>
<span name="5.2.385">That can torment him much and hold him long,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.386">It shall be his. You shall close prisoner rest,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.387">Till that the nature of your fault be known</span><br>
<span name="5.2.388">To the Venetian state. Come, bring him away.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.389">Soft you; a word or two before you go.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.390">I have done the state some service, and they know't.</span><br>
<span name="5.2.391">No more of that. I pray you, in your letters,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.392">When you shall these unlucky deeds relate,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.393">Speak of me as I am; nothing extenuate,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.394">Nor set down aught in malice: then must you speak</span><br>
<span name="5.2.395">Of one that loved not wisely but too well;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.396">Of one not easily jealous, but being wrought</span><br>
<span name="5.2.397">Perplex'd in the extreme; of one whose hand,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.398">Like the base Indian, threw a pearl away</span><br>
<span name="5.2.399">Richer than all his tribe; of one whose subdued eyes,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.400">Albeit unused to the melting mood,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.401">Drop tears as fast as the Arabian trees</span><br>
<span name="5.2.402">Their medicinal gum. Set you down this;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.403">And say besides, that in Aleppo once,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.404">Where a malignant and a turban'd Turk</span><br>
<span name="5.2.405">Beat a Venetian and traduced the state,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.406">I took by the throat the circumcised dog,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.407">And smote him, thus.</span><br>
<p><i>Stabs himself</i></p>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.408">O bloody period!</span><br>
<br>

<b>GRATIANO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.409">                  All that's spoke is marr'd.</span><br>
<br>

<b>OTHELLO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.410">I kiss'd thee ere I kill'd thee: no way but this;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.411">Killing myself, to die upon a kiss.</span><br>
<p><i>Falls on the bed, and dies</i></p>
<br>

<b>CASSIO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.412">This did I fear, but thought he had no weapon;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.413">For he was great of heart.</span><br>
<br>

<b>LODOVICO</b>
<br>
<span name="5.2.414">[To IAGO]  O Spartan dog,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.415">More fell than anguish, hunger, or the sea!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.416">Look on the tragic loading of this bed;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.417">This is thy work: the object poisons sight;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.418">Let it be hid. Gratiano, keep the house,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.419">And seize upon the fortunes of the Moor,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.420">For they succeed on you. To you, lord governor,</span><br>
<span name="5.2.421">Remains the censure of this hellish villain;</span><br>
<span name="5.2.422">The time, the place, the torture: O, enforce it!</span><br>
<span name="5.2.423">Myself will straight aboard: and to the state</span><br>
<span name="5.2.424">This heavy act with heavy heart relate.</span><br>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
